After I had completed for you, sons, this book, which is the last part of science in medicine with its complement, and I had reached the end in it, from its explanations and declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this Treatise, which is a part of operation, that is, surgery with hand.
Because the operation with hand is laid out in our region and time, and has been utterly privatized: so that perhaps the science of it has perished, and its investigation has been cut off: and there did not remain any of it, except for small descriptions in ancient books, which were distorted by hands: and error and hesitation occurred, until the intentions of it were closed, and its force was elongated. It seemed to me that I should revive it with the ordering of this Treatise, according to the way of positioning, declaration, and abbreviation: and so that I might bring it together with the forms of cauterium instruments, and other tools of work: as it is fitting from declarations of addition, and from its proper preparation which is necessary.
The reason why a good craftsman of it with his hand is not found in our time is: because the art of medicine is long and it is necessary for its author to have exercised beforehand in the science of anatomy, which Galen described, so that he may know the juiciness of members, and their forms, and their conjunction, and separation, and have cognition of bones, and nerves, and ligaments, and their number, and their egressions, and veins pulsating, and quiet ones, and exit places.
And on account of this, Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with work is little, and especially in the art of hand.
We have now spoken about it in the introduction of this book.
Because whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said about anatomy will not be cautious, lest they already fall into error, by which men are harmed: just as I have seen many of those who are formed by this science, and boast about it without knowledge, and without experience.
What happened was that a foolish doctor cut into a scrofulous apostem on the neck of a woman and severed certain arteries in her neck, so that her blood flowed out, until she fell dead at his hands.
And another foolish doctor who attempted to extract a stone from a man's testicle, which was swollen at the time, and the stone was large. He therefore approached him, and extracted it along with a piece of his bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And I had already been called in to extract it: and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the sick man that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who received a stipend from a certain Duke of our land because of his medical practice: and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him, that he had a fracture in his leg near the ankle: and the doctor, with his ignorance, treated the fracture with poultices, and bound it tightly with a bandage, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he dismissed him according to his foolish desires. Afterwards he sent him away for several days and instructed him not to remove the bandage: and it remained thus until his leg became infected and his foot, and it led to destruction.
I was therefore called in for him: and I hastened to remove the bandage: and calmness followed, and he was freed from his pains.
However, the corruption had already become established in the limb: and I was not able to restrain it.
So then the corruption ceased to spread through the limb, until he died.
And I saw another doctor who pierced a cancerous apostem: and it became ulcerated after days, until the evil of his lord was magnified with him.
What is, because when there is a pure cancer from melancholic humor, then it does not seem advisable to approach it with iron at all, unless it be in a member that can tolerate it, so that the whole of it may be cut away.
And because of that, O sons, it is necessary for you to know that the operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, an operation associated with salvation, and an operation in which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already pointed out in every place of this book, where an operation comes up, in which there is fear and dread.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of that, and to moderate it: so that the stupid ones may not find a way to speak about it, and to discredit it.
Receive therefore the measurement with solicitude and protection, and your infirmities with facility and firmness, and may you have a better way of proceeding by the grace of God to salvation and laudable succession: and abandon the terrible difficulties of difficult healing: and remove your souls from what makes you fear, so that hesitation may not creep over you in your faith and your comfort.
For it is more remaining to your glory, and more sublime in this world, and afterwards to your quantities.
For Galen indeed has already said so in certain of his admonitions. You do not heal the bad illness: lest you be named a bad doctor.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
First Chapter.
On Cauterization with fire, and Cauterization with acute medicine, chaptered, and arranged from head to feet, and the forms of instruments, and the furnishings of Cauterization: and all that is necessary for the operation.
Second Chapter.
On incision and perforation, phlebotomy and venesection, and wounds: and the extraction of arrowheads, and similar things: and the entire chapter, arranged in the forms of instruments.
The third chapter.
On restoration and dislocation, and the treatment of twisting, and similar things:  chapter, arranged from head to foot, and in the forms of instruments.
But before I discuss the operation with it, it is necessary that I describe the quality of its cauterizations and brandings: and in what complexions they are exhibited.
I say therefore that the discourse on the quality of cauterization by hot iron and its branding is a prolix, subtle, scientific, and hidden secret.
Also, many wise men have spoken about it, and they have disagreed about it: and to me, indeed, a little from their discourses is enough, fearing prolixity.
I say therefore that cauterization is suitable universally for every complexion, which is with matter and without matter: except for two complexions, which are the hot complexion without matter and the dry complexion without matter.
But in the hot and dry complexions with matter, they disagreed. For some said that cauterization is beneficial in them. And others said the opposite, namely that cauterization is not suitable for a illness which arises from hot and dry qualities: since the nature of fire is heat: and it is unsuitable to be healed from a hot and dry illness with hot and dry things.
And he who says the opposite of that said: that through cauterization a remedy is made in every hot and dry affliction that occurs in human bodies; because when you examine the body of a man and its humidity, according to the complexion of fire, you find the body of a man to be cold.
And I say through his discourse: because from my experiments he has already demonstrated that to me many times.
However, it is not proper for him to come forward with that, unless he who has already been tested and exercised in the last chapter of Cauterii's exercise, and has recognized the diversity of human complexions, and the disposition of afflictions within themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and their time span.
But there is no fear from the remaining complexions over you: and especially in cold and moist afflictions. For all physicians have come to an agreement about these: and they do not disagree with Cauterius in their remedies.
And you should know, my sons, that the secret of curing through Cauterium with fire and its goodness is above Cauterium with combusting medicine: because fire is simple, whose action does not reach, unless to the member that is cauterized; and it does not harm another member joined to it, except by a small injury.
However, the action of combusting medicine reaches to that which is extended from the members; and perhaps it causes an affliction to occur in the member that is difficult to heal, and perhaps it interferes.
However, fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it is excessive.
For we have learned that through experience, because of the length of service and study with art, and standing upon the truth of things; and because of that I excuse myself from the length of the discourse.
And if it were not, because it is not permitted to me in this book of mine, I would reveal to you the hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation on bodies through expulsion of their own diseases, which expels diseases by philosophical demonstration, which will be impressed upon your minds.
And you know, my sons, that they disagree among themselves at the time when it is suitable to perform cauterization, and they set a better time for spring.
And I say that cauterization is suitable at any time; because, when a harmful accident occurs due to the season being submerged in youth, which is attracted with cauterization. And especially if cauterization is because of pains from necessary pains, strong, swift, which do not tolerate delay: therefore, because it is feared that a greater evil may occur, which is more than the small harm that occurs at that time.
And do not let it occur to your minds, my sons, that they do not esteem, except the common and foolish physicians, namely that those diseases which are healed by cauterization, are not always a return: and they set forth that consequence, and the thing is not as they think: therefore, because cauterization is not, unless it changes the complexion, and dries out the humidities which are the causes, whence pains occur.
However, cauterization is superior to medicine through the swiftness of its healing, and the virtue of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion: and it is possible that the disease may return at some time according to the complexion of the infirm person, and the location of the disease itself, and its virtue: and what is prepared in his body through an aggregation of superfluous things in it: and what reaches him in his acquisition from foods and similar causes, unless there is a disease for which cauterization is administered.
A subtle numbness in a few limbs that are swollen and moist, such as a burn from a tooth, due to pain, and similar to that, it is possible that the pain does not return to it. But that occurs in a few.
But truly the common speech is wrong, since cauterization is a last resort of medicine, and it's a correct speech: not towards that which they intend in it; because they believe that there is no cure that can be accomplished with medicine, nor with anything else after the use of cauterization.
The reality is contrary to that, and the intention, that cauterization is a last resort of medicine, is not so; unless when we administer methods of cure in some numbness, and they do not confer with those medicines: then we administer cauterization at the end, and it confers; therefore it falls, that cauterization is a last resort of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many stupid doctors understand.
The ancients, however, said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron; and they did not say that, except because of the equality of gold, and the sublimity of its substance: and they said that it does not produce pus at the place of cauterization. That is not absolutely true: because I have already tested that, and found that it does not do that in certain bodies without others.
And cauterization with gold itself is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you heat cauterization fire in a gold fire, it is not declared to you, when it is ignited according to the quantity that you want, because of the redness of the gold: and when it approaches the cold, and if you add ignition on top of it, it melts in the fire and turns into plates.
Therefore the craftsman falls from that into the occupation: and because of that, cauterization with iron is more suitable and closer to us, due to its straightforwardness in operation.
And I have already arranged this chapter on cauterization, following the chapters; and I have arranged it from head to feet, so that they may find quickly what they want from it.
Head 2.
Here cauterization is beneficial for mastering humidity and coldness on the brain, which are two causes of diseases, and many fluxes of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and many sleep disorders, and toothaches, and throat pains; and universally all sicknesses that occur from coldness, such as paralysis, and diseases, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar ones from those sicknesses.
The method of cauterization is to prepare the patient: so that they may be evacuated in the first place with cleansing medicine, purifying the head for three nights or four, according to what the strength of the patient requires, and their age, and their habit.
Then advise them to shave their head with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands squarely, so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Then put the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger touches, mark that place with a cauterization.
Then apply the cautery of olive oil: this is its form.
Then place it over the marked spot with the cautery, descending gradually, as your hand contracts slowly, and you turn it around. Then lift your hand quickly, and inspect the spot.
If you see that it has already drawn out a quantity of brain marrow or a quantity of zeolite, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat with your hand in the same place, or with another from the same place if it becomes cold: until you see the bones, which I told you.
Then apply something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the same cotton, and put it on the location: and leave it there for three days.
Then put the cotton soaked in butter on it, and leave it on the location until the scab is destroyed by fire. Then treat it with four-drug ointment, until it heals.
Some have said that when the wound remains open for a longer time, it discharges pus; therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them have said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone: and the cautery should be held in place until it reaches a certain degree of hardness of the bone.
Then scrape off what has been burned onto the bone, then treat it.
And others say that it is necessary to reach the bone with the cautery until the end, so that it makes an impression on the bone, so that it becomes like a shell shape: or an instrument which women use for inserting small letters: and they think that vapors rise from this place to the head, and the wound should be left open for a long time.
Then treat it, until it consolidates.
But to me, these two methods of cauterization do not seem useful at all, except in certain men according to the way of fear.
And to leave it alone is better for me, with the safety of his own health.
For the head is weakened by the dissolution of its natural continuity: as we have testified to in other members: and especially when the head of the infirm person is weak by nature: and indeed the first species of cauterization is safer and better for me, and I approve it: therefore operate with it for health.
Head 3.
When a chronic pain occurs throughout the whole head, and it is prolonged in the weak, and it uses yawning, and hiccuping, and purging of the head, and anointing with oil, and applying poultices. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, which we have described, and nothing of those things helps it: then consider. For if the head of the weak patient is of a strong natural constitution, and it is not feeble, and it finds a violent cold: then cauterize with another cautery beneath that place a little. Then cauterize him on the entire crown of his head with a cautery, so that it does not penetrate through the skin, and a quantity of bone is disclosed, as we have described. And cauterize him with one cautery on the back of his head, in the place that is called "uas": and it is a place where a vein is located: and elevate your material in this, and do not disclose the bone. For the weak patient finds relief from that violent pain, and is freed from the pain of the remaining cauteries of his entire head.
And I say that this Cautery is in its proper place: and it is necessary that there be a cautery, with which the crowns of the head are cauterized, and his back is more subtly cauterized with a cautery, with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Head 4.
When pain and soreness occur in part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is cleansed with purifying medications, and the remaining treatment is administered, as I said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not help entirely: then cauterization there is according to two methods: either cauterization with a sharp burning medicine, or with iron.
The cauterization is done with acute medicine, burning as you receive one of the teeth of the other, and you excise it, and you cut off its extremities from both sides. Then, you make an incision at the place of pain at the time with a broad scalpel, until it becomes a spot beneath the skin, where the tooth is seized.
Introduce it therefore beneath the skin, until it is hidden: then bind above it with a decent constriction of poultice, and leave it for fifteen hours; then loosen it, and extract the tooth, and leave it for two days, or three. Afterwards, put above it a submerged cotym covered in butter, until the place makes pus: then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish to do that with certain burning medicines, which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise, concerning medicines that draw out.
The cauterization is indeed done with iron, according to this method. A fiery cauterization, whose form is this.
And it is named Clavulus; because the form of its head is like the form of a little nail, in which there is some curvature, and in its middle there is a small prominence.
Then put it on the spot, and hold your hand firm; and you rotate the iron slowly with speed: and let the amount that is burned be from the thickness of the skin, as its middle. And lift your hand, so that the artery which is below is not burned, and a flow of blood occurs.
Then soak the cotym in salt water, and put it on the spot, and leave it for three days: then put the cotym with butter: afterwards treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this half of the skull with the secondary edge of the scalpel's cauterization. And beware of cutting into an artery in this half-cranium, not in the ancient proper way.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the ancient half-cranium.
When you treat a half-cranium, with what we have said from previous cures and what we have said in divisions of illnesses, and the cure does not work: and you see from the illness that it does not suffice for him what we have said from the first cauterization with medicine, or with cauterization with fire, then it is necessary to apply a burning cauterization, until it becomes white after marking the place of pain with a line, whose length should be half a finger, or nearly so: and put your hand in place of one, and press it down until you cut into an artery, and penetrate to the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuation of the jawbone, which moves during mastication, lest it be dislocated, or the nerve that moves it, whence a spasm occurs.
And this is above the joint, and beware of the flow of blood from the artery, which has been cut off. For in cutting it off, there is fear, and especially for him who does not know what he is doing, and is not diligent, nor experienced: and he leaves the operation with this at the beginning.
And I come with a reminder of the rule for controlling the flow of blood that occurs from an artery according to its own method, and in its place in this book.
What if you see from the illness that this cauterization does not suffice for him, and you see the weak body tolerating the cauterization in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, cure the wound, until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer a cauterization, which we have said in the chapter on extracting an artery with a cauterization having two burning irons. For cauterization is better and more beneficial in this case.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in painful ear infections.
When pain in the ear occurs from cold, and it is treated with solutives, and other treatments that we mentioned earlier, and the pain does not subside, then cauterization by fire is applied: and this is what is called a Punctum, whose shape is as follows.
Then the punctures are made with it around the entire ear after its ignition, as it revolves: or around both ears, if there is pain in both. And stretch it out with the cauterizing iron at the root of the ear for a short time, after you have marked the places with ink: and let the quantity of the cauterization be ten punctures on each ear, or almost so.
Then treat the places until they heal.
Concerning the method of cauterizing for tetanus.
Chapter 7.
The tetanus that is treated with cauterization is not except for those cases which occur from phlegmatic causes, according to what we said in the divisions of diseases.
And it is necessary to apply cauterization to the type that occurs from dryness and nervous spasm.
When you treat this type of tetanus with hiera, and head purging, and gargling, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient in three places: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little below the temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And apply your cauterizing iron from the opposite side of the affected part. For softening does not occur except in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is to cauterize it with the cauterizing iron directly on the upper extremity of the ear below the crown of the head, a little above the temple: and another on the same side, whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And put your hand with a cautery until it burns to the extent of the moderate thickness of the skin.
And this is the form of a Cautery, and it is a type from a small knife, whose form is previously mentioned: however it is not too subtle, as you see; and it is necessary that the small knife be above a little bit of excessive thickness.
Then treat the place with what has preceded: until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in ancient Apoplexy.
When ancient Apoplexy is antiquated, and you treat it with what we have said, and your medication does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every horn of his head, and a cautery in the middle of the head, as we have said, and a cautery at the back of the head, according to what has preceded: and the method of the cautery should be according to what has preceded.
He is also cauterized with a cautery on the bone of the stomach: and it is even more extreme.
Then he should be treated with what has preceded.
Chapter 9.
It is necessary that the drink be given first to the sick person with great hysteria, and purifying pills for cleansing the brain.
Then shave the whole head of the sick person, and put on his occiput a Synapic plaster described in the treatise on plasters: and put it on several times.
This indeed is the method of the Cautery: and do that according to the same order which I mentioned there.
If he is thus healed through that, it is good. If not: then make for him three cauteries on the back of his head, which should descend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye: and put a thickness of a finger between each cautery.
Then treat the cauterization, with what has preceded it.
If however there is an addition and he is weakened, bearing that: then make a cauterization for him in the middle. What if there is an addition: then cauterize it above the two horns.
Then treat him, until he is healed: and let the cauterization be according to the second form, which has been mentioned before.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter 10.
It is necessary to proceed with cleansing the head with yolks of eggs, and with what we have said.
Then shave the head of the invalid: afterwards cauterize him with a cauterization in the middle of the head, and with a cauterization above every horn of the head, and with a cauterization above the nape of his neck, and three on the vertebrae of the neck.
If however you find him in a severe softening of the body from many of those, and he is weakened, bearing that, and the disease is strong: then cauterize him with four cauterizations on the vertebrae of the back, and finally with a cauterization, until it burns deeply into his skin, and lift your hand. Then treat him, until he is healed: and thus the cauterization is to be made with olive oil.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
The epileptic is not to be cauterized, unless it is he whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
It is necessary therefore to cleanse his brain first with yolks of eggs, and with the remaining treatment which we mentioned earlier: when he is greatly weakened, or bears it in the acceptance of medicines.
If however he is a boy who does not tolerate medicines, then let him be given gargles and cleansing mastications for the brain, before that for many days with a blessing of foods.
Then shave the top of his head, afterwards cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what has been described previously; and with another cautery on its occiput, and over the entire horn-shaped part of his head with a cautery. What if the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries that I mentioned in the case of one having paralysis, and mollification of the body on the vertebrae of the neck, and the vertebrae of the back; and let the cautery be oily according to the method that has been described previously.
If however the patient is a child, then apply a subtle cautery, according to this method.
On the method of cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries that we mentioned in the case of one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an abundance of fluids inclined towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him a drink that will cleanse his brain, according to what has been described previously in the division: then shave the head of the patient, and afterwards make a well-made tortellum from linen, like a circle.
Then put it on the middle of his head: and let the patient, sitting squarely, be held firmly from all sides.
Then apply the liniment. And it is more worthy to use old butter or ancient oil. And heat it over a fire with a tempered measure of heat, which the finger can tolerate, when it is inserted into it. Then evacuate it on the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools down.
Do that to the patient every week once, with the rest of his good regime, until he is healed.
If you wish, burn him by making many small points with the cautery, taking care not to hold your hand too tightly on the cautery: namely, while smelling it.
For this type of cautery humidifies the brain with its quality.
Then put on top of it a cloth imbued with butter, or the fat of a hen.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in descending water to the eye.
Chapter 13.
When the principle of water in the eye is declared to you through signs, which I mentioned in the division, then begin and cleanse the weak part, together with what purifies his head.
And keep it away from all moistures, and make him sit in a bath, on fasting days for some time.
Then instruct him to shave his head, and to cauterize it in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him above the two temples with two cauteries, if there is a downward flow of water in both eyes at the same time: or from one side, if there is a flow of water in one eye: and cut off all the veins and arteries that are beneath the skin with the cautery: and let the cauteries be long in width across the temples: and beware of a flux of blood.
If you see anything coming out of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I warn with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting off, and caution against a flux of blood.
And when it is cauterized on the neck, beneath the two bones, with two cauteries produced to the utmost extent.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and frequent: and they are above the veins and arteries that are on the outer surface of the head, it is verified that it is from cold and phlegmatic superfluities: then cauterize with the cautery which I described in the flow of descending water, with a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries on the neck beneath the two bones. And if you notice an excess, then cauterize it on every side of the eye, above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
On the method of cauterizing in the nasal fossa.
When you treat it, with what we said in the division, and the treatment does not help: then prepare, and give a potion of three nights to the weak-sighted; afterwards shave their head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with an oily cautery. Then cauterize it with two nail-shaped cauterizers, above the two eyebrows, beneath the hair, a little.
And be cautious of the artery, lest you wound it.
And this is the shape of a nail-shaped cautery.
On the method of cauterizing in the relaxation of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is relaxed from sickness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this lunar-shaped cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on every side; and they will be lengthened from two temporal areas; and let the entire length of the cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not finally move your hand with the cautery, but rather according to the quantity that touches the third eyelid.
On the method of cauterizing an eyelid when hairs are embedded that pierce the eye.
The cautery is of two kinds: either a cautery with fire, or a cautery with burning medicine.
With the cautery of fire, warn the weak patient beforehand, so that they may release their hairs, if they are among those who clean them, until they grow long and equal. If they sting him at his own door, then bind his eyes with a cloth, so that they do not move until they are fully opened.
When they have opened and are equalized, then place the head of the afflicted one in your lap; afterwards, mark above his eyelids with a cautery, marking what is according to the shape of the myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then put a bandage soaked in white egg or in a mucilage of psyllium over the eye.
Then apply a cautery of fire, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the shape that you marked gradually in many places, until the surface of the skin is burned, which is like the shape of the myrtle leaf, making it appear properly whole.
And the sign of the success of your work is this: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted, and the hairs lifted up at the point of the eye.
Lift your hand then, and leave it for three days.
Then put a bandage with butter on it, until the scab is eradicated. Then treat it with an ointment, until it is healed.
If something returns from the hairs after that hour and the eyelid becomes soft, then apply the cautery again to that place, just as you did at first.
If the hairs are below, then cauterize them, until they lift up to their natural place: and equalize them so that they do not sting the eye.
It is as if you instruct the afflicted one to let the hairs grow, until they lengthen and equalize. Make a shape of the myrtle leaf from a paper template.
Then take from known soap and from unsoaked lime a pound and a half or nearly that amount; then grind those things together with good contraction, and make it with thorough mixing, so that it is not frozen. Then take from the pan the same amount that you made into a shape like a myrtle leaf, and put it on the eyelid of one eye or of two. And put under the eye a small piece of cloth soaked in white egg, and let the head of the injured person be in your lap.
And put your index finger on the medicine, and press it gently for a while. And you move it around whenever the injured person feels the biting of the medicine, because he finds its biting like fire.
While therefore it perseveres this which he himself has found the biting, then remove the medicine, and move it around with your finger. When therefore the biting subsides, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And consider then, if you see the eyelid being elevated, as it is elevated by contraction with fire or with incision, it is good: and if not, then repeat over the same place from the medicine, where the medicine does not impress, and does not stain, until your operation is equalized, and the eye is contracted.
Then put over it a small piece of cloth with butter, until the skin is freed from burning. Then treat it with a diaphenic ointment or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to keep a final guard, lest something from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid becomes soft after a few days, and something struggles from the hairs into the eye, then repeat the medicine over that place which becomes soft from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it, until it heals.
And this is the form of myrtle leaves.
And you should know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that, let your consideration be: and the way of righteousness is not hidden from him who has a zeal for this art.
On the method of cautery on the tear duct fistula.
When you treat the fistula, with that which we mentioned in the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not help: then, it is necessary to cauterize it according to this method.
Order the patient to put his head on your lap, and let his servant hold his head between their hands in such a way that it is not moved or stirred with his own head.
Then put a cloth soaked in egg white or a poultice of powdered psyllium over his eye: then ignite the cautery iron, whose form is this.
It should be a concave shape, like the form of a feather's quill from one extremity, with which the cautery is made: and if you wish it to penetrate up to the other extremity, and if you wish it to be bent upwards in this way.
However, this concave shape is better suited for your work.
Then squeeze out the fistula, if it is open, and extract from it the sanious matter, and cleanse it: and if it is not open, then open it, and extract its pus.
Then put the cautery iron, which has been ignited strongly, on top of it.
And hold your hand with it for a short time near the cautery iron, away from the eye, towards the nose, so that your hand does not tremble or disturb the patient: and you will put the cautery iron in the fat of the eye and corrupt it.
If you therefore penetrate at the beginning of the cauterization up to the bone, it will be well. And if not: then repeat the cauterization once or twice, if it is necessary for that; and let it be left for three days.
Then put a dressing with butter, and take care of it with a stimulating ointment, until it heals.
If it has passed forty days and it does not heal: then put on top of it a sharp corroding medicine, until the bone is exposed; and scrape it according to what is written in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some first authorities have mentioned. Direct yourself to the place of the fistula and find it; then put into that fissure a subtle cannula, whose shape is this. And pour into it a quantity of drachmae from liquefied lead, and hold your hand with good cannula retention, and do not move the weak one at all, so that it does not flow, or the liquefied lead reaches its eye.
And it is necessary to put on the weak eye a dressing soaked in white egg, or in water.
For the lead indeed burns the place of the fistula, and heals it with a marvelous healing.
If the fistula is healed, along with what we have said about cauterization and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nasal passage, and reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what is suitable for its own place.
On the method of cauterizing in labial fissures.
Fissures often occur on the lip, which are called Pili, and especially on the lips of children.
When you treat these fissures, with what we have said in the division of diseases, and treatment does not help, then make a small cautery iron in the shape of a scalpel.
And let its concavity be according to the subtlety of the scalpel.
Then place it ignited hastily in those fissures, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with a poultice, until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing a fistula of the mouth.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gums, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus, and bursts forth: afterwards it becomes chronic, and a flow of pus ensues, and a fistula forms: then you should treat it, and if it does not respond to treatment, it is necessary to apply a cautery according to its size, which should encompass the fistula. Then insert the ignited iron into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand steady, until the ignited iron reaches the depth of it and its extremity: do that once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we have said about treatment, until it is cured.
If therefore the pus is cut off and heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to lay bare the location, and to remove the corrupted bone according to what appears in its head.
On the method of cauterizing swollen gums and teeth.
When the gums are swollen due to moisture, and the teeth are loose, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not respond: then place the head of the patient in your lap.
Then prepare a cautery, whose form will appear afterwards, so that you place a tube over the tooth: and insert the ignited cautery hastily into it: and hold your hand steady for a little while, until the patient feels the heat of the fire having reached the root of the tooth.
And elevate your hand: then again Cauterium several times, according to what you wish.
Then the weak member soaks its bone in salt water, and holds it for one hour: and extracts it.
For the movement is strengthened, and the gum softened by the string is tightened, and the corrupted humidity is dried.
On the method of cauterizing painful teeth.
When toothache is due to coldness, either the cold is in it or worm, and treatment with medicines does not help: then Cautery is applied to it in two ways: either Cautery with butter or Cautery with fire.
The Cautery with butter is however, that you take clarified butter, and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a vase. Then take cotton, and apply it to the extremity of the tooth. Then submerge it in the boiled butter: and place it quickly on the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools down: then repeat it several times, until the power of fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool, or cotton in cold butter, and place it on the painful tooth: and place ignited iron on top of it, until the fire reaches the depth of the tooth's concavity.
The Cautery with fire is however, that you direct it to a copper tube, or an iron tube. And let there be in its body some thickness, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the weak mouth.
Then apply the fire Cautery, whose form appears: and place it on that tooth: and hold your hand until the Cautery cools down.
Do that several times, for the pain is removed, either on that same day, or another day.
And it is necessary in the impression of that cautery, to fill the weakened bone with good pus, and to hold it for one hour; then to evacuate it.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with a hot iron on whatever extremity you use, according to what is possible; and this is the form of the cannula.
On the method of cautery in Scrofula.
When Scrofula are from phlegm, and from cold humidities, and are not obedient to digestion through medicines, and you wish to hasten their digestion: then apply a concave cautery fire, whose form is this.
It has two open extremities, so that the smoke may emerge from the cautery at the other extremity: and place it ignited upon the aposteme once, and a second time, if it is necessary, until it reaches the depth of the aposteme.
If the aposteme is small: then place the cautery according to the quantity of the aposteme.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a cloth infused with butter, until what was burned by the fire is removed.
Then treat it with a denti's ointment, until the form of the cannula heals.
On the method of cautery on a hoarse voice and constricted breathing.
When humidities overcome the pulmonary canal, and especially when it is with a cold complexion, then it is necessary to evacuate the weakened area first with dissolving medicines.
Then cautery it at night beside the root of the throat in a depressed place: and beware, lest you penetrate with the cautery to the throat, or in the skin, unless something of it.
Then cautery it with another cautery at the joint of the neck in its last vertebra: and let the cautery be a moderate one according to the method that preceded.
Then treat him with what came before until he is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of lung inflammation and cough.
When cough and lung inflammation are caused by cold humidities, and the patient is not feverish, nor consumptive, and the illness is not chronic: then cauterize him with two cauterizations above the ankle in depressed, slack, and empty places. And cauterize with another on the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cauterization be according to the shape of the tube which came before.
And if you wish to cauterize by pricking with the cauterization tool, which is called a Point, whose shape came before in the pricking of the pain of the ears: and let there be points from thirty points up to almost sixty.
Then treat him with what came before until he is healed.
And now let the cauterization instrument have three branches: according to this shape. Because it is alleviated with that cauterization when you make it into one of the three Cauterizations.
Chapter 27.
When the head of the joint is dislocated due to humid causes, and it does not return to its place at once after its dislocation, until it becomes accustomed to returning to its own location, then it is dislocated by a small motion, which occurs as we have already demonstrated, then you should reduce the dislocation first. Then the patient should be placed on his back or on his healthy side. Then elevate the skin which is on the inside of the shoulder to the top with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint is dislocated inward.
Then apply a cauterization instrument having two rods. This form is this.
Then cauterize the wound, until it penetrates to another side, and there will be a figure of cauterization with four cauteries.
And when a cauterization is made with a cautery having three arms, then the figure of cauterization will be of six cauteries; and they are arms according to the subtlety of the tension.
And this is the form of a cautery having three arms.
And when one is added in this way, then there are eight cauteries.
Then put rough salt on the cautery that has been contracted. Then make the weak part adhere to tranquility, so that the limb is not moved for some time, until it is comforted.
And if the dislocation is towards the upper parts, and this rarely happens, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a cautery of claws, or with multiple points.
For the joint is strengthened, and moisture is removed: and the weak part is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the Stomach.
When cold and many humidities accumulate in the Stomach, until they extract it from its natural complexion, and multiply the fluxes to it, and assiduous methods of cure do not help: then it is necessary that the weak part be supported on its back, and stretch out its legs, and hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery under the spoon-shaped part of the chest in the quantity of one finger, and two cauteries below from the two sides of the cautery, until there appears a triangular figure of cauteries. And stretch out between both, so that they do not join together, when they make pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the quantity of two thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of cauteries be according to this form without addition; and if you wish to cauterize with a large cauterizing instrument in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and let the cauterizing instrument be one according to the circular figure according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking him who is terrified by this cautery; and it is, as you mark on the stomach a point according to the quantity that you wish with an encaustic; then cauterize it with the cautery of the point; then cure it with the treatment that precedes until he is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a cold Epiploic (fatty) appendix.
When there is pain in the liver due to coldness and humidity, or due to coarse flatulence, until it departs from its natural passage and the sick person becomes weak, as we have said, and does not benefit from it: then it is necessary for the sick person to be placed on their back, and marked with three cauteries according to this figure, and in the same quantity on the lower liver below the ribs, where the elbow of a man reaches; and let there be space between each cauterization according to the thickness of the finger: and let the cauterizing instrument be straight according to the length of the body: and do not press your hand too much with the cauterizing instrument.
And let the quantity of it that is touched be according to the thickness of the skin, a moderate quantity not added; and let the sick person stand on their own feet.
But if they are not standing, then let them lie down, who has already stretched out their legs and raised their arms.
This is the shape of the cautery.
And it is indeed possible for you to cauterize with this cautery using a knife-shaped cautery, when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And beware lest you proceed to the extreme in cauterization, and the hardness of the entire skin is scorched, because it scorches the entire body, and reaches to the intestines; for the skin there is subtle, so know that.
On the method of cauterizing apostemes of the liver.
When an aposteme occurs, and you want to know if that aposteme is in the flesh of the liver or in its membrane: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, it produces a dull pain and heaviness without acuteness: and if it is in the membrane of the liver, with pain there is vehement acuteness: and you see already, because it has exhausted the doctors with its treatment.
It is necessary therefore that the weak person takes a rest on his couch. Then mark out the place of the aposteme with encaustic: then apply a cautery that is similar to a star. And this is its shape. And cauterize with one cautery until the entire skin is burned, and reaches to the vitellus, until all the sanies are discharged: then take care of the same curation of apostemes, until it is healed.
And it is not fitting that one uses this type of cautery, unless one whose study in the medical art is prolonged: and through whose hands these diseases converge with some experimentation many times: then indeed he dares to undertake such an operation.
But truly to omit it, it is better in my opinion.
On the method of cauterizing in cases of Pleurisy.
The ancients said that a cautery with the roots of Aristolochia is beneficial for cold Pleurisy in this manner. And it is, that you take from the dry roots of Aristolochia a root, one longer than the others, which is found to be as thick as a finger. Then submerge it in oil and set it on fire. Then cauterize with a single cauterization at the point where the gullet meets the neck, and with two small cauteries under the guidance of small inclinations towards the part that is beneath the beard.
And with two cauteries also at the point that is between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclining towards the back a little; and with one cauterization in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the back: one at the point that is between the two shoulder blades; and with two cauteries on both sides of the chest, the lower cauterization being between the two shoulder blades.
And it is not necessary to compress your hand with the cauterization, but rather let it be on the manifest skin, emitting an odour.
And now certain ancients have said that there are those who use cauterization with an iron instrument similar to a rod; and they ignite it, and insert it between the ribs until it reaches the aposteme itself, and the sanies flow out: as we have described in the case of Epatis' aposteme.
But in this perforation with a cauterization there is fear, lest the weak patient dies immediately, or a fistula occurs at that place, which has no healing.
On the method of cauterizing the Spleen, Chapter XXXII.
When you treat an illness of the spleen, with what we have said about cures in the division of illnesses, and your treatment does not work, then cauterization is used in three ways, all of which are correct.
One of which is to make three or four cauteries in a line along the length of the spleen, according to the figure of the cauteries of Epatis, whose figure has preceded.
And let there be between each cauterization a quantity of thickness equal to that of a finger, or a little more.
And this is the method of cautery, which we have described in the cautery of the liver, done equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: and let the patient lie down on his back.
And another method of cauteration is: to hold the two-pronged cautery, which we have described in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder; and elevate the skin, which is on the direct splenetic line, where the cubit of the left arm reaches; and let your elevation be such that you elevate the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then introduce the two-pronged ignited cautery, until you penetrate the skin on the other side: then withdraw the cautery: thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with a cautery having three prongs.
Then take care to apply the cautery after you have released it, to bring forth pus for many days: for it is more beneficial than the rest that preceded in the cure.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Dropsy.
The cautery does not fall in Dropsy, unless applied precisely.
When you treat a Dropsical patient with the methods of cure that we have described in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery above the stomach, and another above the liver, and one on the spleen, and two on the back between the vertebrae, and one on the direct line of the chest, and another on the direct line of the stomach: and let the depth of the cautery be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the open cautery, so that it brings forth pus for a long time.
And do not evacuate the patient from the cure after the cautery with it: for it is necessary that two intentions are added to him: and he will be hastened to his healing with the help of God.
The shape of the cautery iron with which the belly is cauterized should be club-shaped: according to the preceding shape of it; and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped according to the preceding shape of it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When they swell with hydroptic dropsy and are filled with citrine water: it is necessary to cauterize on the upper part of the foot at night, which is between the anklebone and the ring finger; and raise your hand with the cautery iron, and do not twist it; then raise your hand, and do not repeat it at all.
For the citrine water flows back, and the cautery iron should be according to this shape.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery iron be at the end of the knife-shaped cautery; and let it be according to the length of the leg, one below the knee, and another lower than that, around the middle of the leg; and above all the hip, two cauteries; and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time: so that some water may flow out from it; then treat it with the rest as we have said.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the case of a ruptured belly.
Chapter 35.
When there is a rupture of the belly due to cold and humidity, until it weakens the retentive and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestines; and it is treated with methods of treatment, but not healed; and you see an infirm person tolerating a cautery of overflowing virtue, then cauterize it with a large cautery iron on their belly, according to what precedes in cauterizing the stomach with a circular cautery iron, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a club-shaped subtle cautery; and with a cautery above the groins above the hips with a large one, or with two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moistness, and the weak patient tolerates that, then cauterize it with a cautery on the pubic area, and cauterize all of that with a cautery: and perhaps add two small cauterizations on the stomach near the large one.
It is a profitable treatment, whose benefit does not fail.
On the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter 36.
When there are old and numerous hemorrhoids in the anus, or one, and they are from gross, cold, or corrupt humors, and are treated with what we said earlier, but the treatment does not help: then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower vertebra of the back below the waist, almost triangularly, and with a cautery near the navel, about two fingers wide.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food does not digest, and you see his face affected with aposteme, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery, according to what has been said before: and with a cautery on his liver, and another on his spleen, with a cautery of the claws: and leave the cautery open for some time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter 37.
When you have surgically removed the ulcers, then apply a fiery cautery that is similar to a spark. Then insert the ignited cautery into the surgically removed ulcer: and ultimately with your hand, until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, from which the blood flows: do it once or twice.
If there are many ulcers, then cauterize each one with a cautery according to what we have narrated. Then treat them with what is beneficial to them from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize him with a large cautery on the shoulder blade, it is more effective in the joint.
On the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter 38.
When the sick person does not obey the treatment and operation that we have described in its proper place, and is troubled by it, perhaps he may be healed with a cautery.
When therefore a fistula happens to someone, and it becomes chronic, pus flows out of it, and the corrupted moisture ferments. It is more dignified therefore that what is fitting should be done, so that you may probe it with a subtle probe. Then recognize the quantity of its depth with the probe.
Then apply a cautery, which is similar to a rod. Then insert the ignited cautery itself into the fistula and the quantity where the nail went in.
And repeat over it the cautery, until all the corrupted bodily parts are burned away, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of your necessary treatment.
And be cautious of the nerve's burning, if it is there, or of the great veins; or if the fistula reaches to the bladder or to the intestine, then beware of all these places.
And do not do that unless the fistula is in a fleshy place; and consider that it does not penetrate.
Then take care of the place until it is healed.
If however the place is sealed, and the materials are cut off from it, and it remains so for a long time; then know that it has already been fully healed.
And if the materials do not cut off from it, then know that it is penetrating, or there is a corrupted opening deep within it, or something like that among them; whose reminder will come in its proper place.
On the method of cauterizing Kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys due to cold or excessive flatulence, and it is diminished because of that weak condition, then it is necessary to cauterize it above the loins, to cauterize each kidney with a cautery claw, whose preceding memory.
And perhaps we should cauterize it secondly in that very loin itself. Because three lines are drawn. Therefore they will be more effective in the treatment.
On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness occurs in the bladder due to cold and humidity, until it does not retain the urine of the weak person, then cauterize it on the lower part of the back above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic region begin, and with a cautery from the right side of the back, and another from the left side: and let the length of that cautery be according to the size of the knot of the thumb: and cauterize it with a lower dorsal cautery, or with two cauteries if needed, and let it be according to what precedes the claw-like cautery.
On the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and humidity occur in the womb, and it is prevented by that from becoming pregnant, and its menses are corrupted, and their provocation is delayed, and pain occurs to her upon their arrival, then it is necessary to cauterize with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a cautery above the lower back, or with two cauteries: and let the claw-like cautery be used.
On the method of cauterizing the ankle in dislocation.
When mucous humidity flows to the hollow of the ankle, and becomes the cause of its exit from its place: and the sign of this is that the leg is prolonged above the other when they are compared to each other: and the location of the dislocation is found empty.
Therefore, it is necessary to cauterize the weak area above the ankle with a cautery similar to the circle of the ankle; after you mark out the circumference of the ankle with an encaustic, as it revolves: and so that the very pixy falls in the middle of the circle.
What if this cautery is not present to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large oily cautery: and let the depth of the cautery be according to the quantity of the thickness of the entire skin.
Then treat it, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing for sciatica.
When pain occurs in the ankle, and the causes of it are cold and moisture: and the weak area is treated with what we mentioned earlier, and treatment does not help, and it gets worse: then it is necessary to free the weak area from thick humors with foul-smelling poultices, or with artificial poultices, and similar things. Then cauterize it.
And the method of cautery for it is according to two modes: either cautery with adhering medications, or cautery with fire.
Cautery with fire is according to many modes.
One of which is to cauterize above the ankle with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make their depth good or bad. And let the space that is between each cautery be of the quantity of the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be oily.
When, however, a cautery is made in the middle above the head of the ankle itself. Because there are four cauteries.
And if you want to cauterize with a circle, whose form has preceded in the cauterization of dislocation of the ankle, one: so that it is a circle containing the entire ankle.
And burn the thickness of the whole skin.
This is the method of cauterization in sciatica, when the pain adheres to the anchaea itself and does not extend to the hip and leg.
If it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries above the hip, above the place where the pain is, in which there is pain, and with your cautery on the neck of the thigh four fingers' width towards the wooded part for a short time: and let the cautery be a knife-shaped one.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
What if the pain indicates that the pain extends almost to the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where it indicates with a cautery of one point, three points, or four points, or more, if it needs it.
And if it indicates that the pain is beneath the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with a single knife-shaped cautery.
And be careful in all your cauterizations, so that you do not ultimately harm with the cautery to the point of burning a nerve or a large artery, and attracting through it a serious bad injury or contraction.
And I have indeed already seen one or another among those who cauterized above the thigh and ultimately harmed in the cauterization, and the leg became inflamed, until a tumor followed to the foot, and the whole foot was perforated and corrupted: then afterwards there occurred a discharge of pus, and death after that.
What if the pain is in two parts at once, cauterize each according to this method.
And certain wise men have said that in cauterizing the anchaea, whose method of cautery is this. Make a similar iron instrument, whose diameter is half a palm: and let it be at its orifice according to the thickness of the core of the finger, or slightly less: and within that instrument let there be a third instrument.
And let there be a space that is between all the veins by the quantity of the node of the thumb; and let the veins be opened from two parts; and let their height be like a knot, or two knots; and make for them a handle from iron, decently adapted in the veins.
Then it is heated in the fire until it becomes red-hot and shoots out sparks; then it is placed on a pillow or cushion with an injured limb resting on a healthy side. Burn him therefore with three rounded cauteries in one vein.
Then leave it alone for three days. Afterwards, apply a plaster with butter; and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
Albucasis said, "We have used this type of cautery little, on account of the terror of its appearance; and for this reason, we have found few who dare to try it out.
However, it is one of the good cauteries for him who endures it, and finds its place with it.
The cautery, however, is with medicines that are suitable, so that you make two veins having a perforated armlet, in which descends the hinge of its gate made of copper or iron, with a length equal to the wall; of which there should be two knots, or almost like them.
And let there be a space that is between the two quantities of the thickness of the finger, and let them be open above and below; and let it be what contains itself according to this form.
Then place it on a pillow or cushion with the injured limb lying on a healthy side. And press your hand strongly on the pillow or cushion. Then pour between two circles of hot water, which has been warmed with fire for a short time, and hold it for the duration of an hour; and let the injured person tolerate its bite and his own burning, for he finds the biting as fire, until the biting ceases.
Then wash your hand with a instrument and remove warm water from the entire limb with sweet water; then let it sit for three days.
And put butter on it, until the blackness of the burn is removed; and let it sit for several days, and then clean out the pus from it. It is indeed the last stage of the treatment.
Then treat it with ointments, until it heals.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg, make a plaster for it with water, according to what you did equally on the limb.
And this is the method of warm water; and I have already written about it in the treatise on medicinal rectifications. Take alkaline and non-extinguished lime of each one part: grind both, and put them in a new pot, whose lower part is perforated with a small hole, according to the quantity that can be poured in as a radius; and place beneath the base of the pot another pot, treated thus: and pour over the alkaline and lime from sweet water, which submerges both by a finger's width; then compress it with your hand with good pressure: and let the pot sit, until the sharp water descends to the lower part of the treated pot.
Then collect all that water, and pour it over another lime; and strain, until it is renewed.
For that will be a strong sharpness then, which is administered in many medical operations and in the cauterization of remaining limbs. Because it produces the operation of fire itself.
And they are among the medicines, with which limbs are cauterized, also like tetany, and honey of apricot, and lime with soap, so that both may be thoroughly mixed.
And Galen indeed reported that a certain man from the ancients was cured by a treatment, by which he was healed of pain in his limb and sciatic vein; and he magnified its effectiveness greatly. And he said that he did not need another treatment, and that he was healed from one vein, since it had been restored, because perhaps he himself had inserted a blocked bath, and had gone out already healed from it.
And it is, that he should be treated with a green poultice: and if a green one is not found, a dry fresh one should be applied; and it should be repeated many times with some fat, and placed on the affected area, where there is pain, or in the leg, or in the hip: and it should be bound, and left for three hours, or for as long as he feels the relief of the burning sensation. Then introduce him to a bath.
When therefore his body becomes very cold, introduce him to the sun. For the pain subsides, and he is healed.
And know that it is not fitting to use any cautery with these medicines, unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides, who said that the dung of goats, when with it a vein is cauterized for sciatica, helps him; and it becomes a cautery according to this method. Let wool be applied, and it be soaked in old oil, and placed on the deep area which is between the thumb of the foot and the ankle, and is closest to the ankle.
Then take dry goat dung, and set it on fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then repeat that. Do not cease to do that, until the sensation reaches the ankle through the middle, and the pain subsides.
And this method of cautery is called Cautery of Goat's Dung.
Of the cautery for pain in the back.
When pain occurs in the back from many causes, either from a fall, or a blow, or excessive evacuation, and similar things, from an infusion of cold and humid matter; and indeed cautery does not fail, except in this one species alone, which is caused by an infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after evacuation of the patient with foul suppurating sores and similar ones, three lines according to the width of the ulcer itself should be made on the back where the pain is, after marking with ink in each line five cauteries or more according to the amount that comes from the tolerance of the patient's strength; and cauterization should be done with caution punctures.
And if you wish, cauterize with three cauteries or four, with a medial cautery claw, according to this method.
Concerning the method of cauterizing on the gibbosity of the navel.
This illness often occurs in small children.
And the sign of this illness in children is that it occurs with a constriction in the breathing upon elevation, and movement; and you will find it in the last vertebra of the back and its nodes, which already begin to emerge above the remaining vertebrae.
When you see that and want to do it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is circular in shape according to this method.
And let the cautery grasp equally over every part of the vertebrae; and if you want to cauterize around the vertebrae with a point-cautery, make two lines or three, and let the points be close together.
Then treat the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, lest you administer the cautery to the gibbosity, which is caused by a spasm of the nerve.
Concerning the method of cauterizing for gout and joint pains.
When joint pains are caused by cold humidities that flow to whatever members of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is customary for doctors to call it Gout specifically.
Since the treatment of cold gouty causes with methods of cure does not remove the pains, then cauterization removes them.
And it is, as he is cauterized after evacuating the surrounding joint of the foot with many cauteries; and let the cautery be oily.
And if you need to make points on the surface of the foot, then make them with a cautery point. What if the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and it often happens that, then cauterize it on every knee with three cauteries, or four from each part, with the same cautery of Clavus.
If however more are needed for you with this cautery, then cauterize it. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, but rather let it be around the thickness of the skin only.
If however the pains ascend to the knees and back, then administer what we said from the cautery in its chapter.
What if the pains are only in the hands, then make points around the joints of the fingers, as two lines encircle.
If however some pain remains in the toes, then make points on every node of a toe, and on the heel of the hand.
If however the pains ascend after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both from every part.
And do not evacuate the weak patient from good regimen, from receiving medications. For if a good regimen is done, and the phlegm is evacuated, he will be healed with the help of God along with this cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in hernias.
When a hernia occurs in the groin, and the intestine descends, or the scrotum to the testicle, and it is beginning to be near: then it is necessary that you should advise the patient to omit digestion on his day. And let it be opened gently, so that pus descends from its own belly.
Then place it between your hands on its back, and instruct it to hold its breath until it goes out, or shows a bubble, or intestine.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark it with a branding iron under the fracture on the bone of the chest, with a mark whose extremity is similar to the middle of a circle at the upper body.
Then apply a branding iron, which has this shape, until it produces a white spot, and pushes out the tiny fragments. Then reduce the intestine, or bubble, to its concavity. Then the assistant should place their hand on the spot, so that the intestine does not come out: and you have now opened between the thighs of the patient, and placed a pillow under them, and one servant is above their thighs, and another above their chest who holds their hands.
Then place the branding iron on the spot, with your hand holding the branding iron straight and steady. And hold it, until you reach the bone: or try again with another vice, if you have not succeeded with it at first until you reach the bone.
And carefully observe the intestine's exit during your branding operation, lest you burn it, and it becomes a fatal wound to the patient, or a great evil.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the branding iron, your operation is of no use.
And it is necessary for the branding iron to be subtle and adapted to the size of the children.
Then take care with the remaining ointments, until they are healed.
And let the patient lie on their back for forty days, until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary to put his nourishment in accordance with the length of time of his cure, so that it soothes his belly: lest the intestine comes out through straining and evacuation.
Then when you want to operate after forty days, then administer a bandage made in the meantime, and keep it for forty days more.
And let him be at rest from labor, and replenished with food and drink, and relieved of violent evacuations.
For when he uses this regimen, he will be healed with a complete healing.
And I will describe the treatment of hernias with an incision in its chapter.
When hernias occur in the rest of the abdomen, and are beginning, and it seems as though they do not add, then cauterize that hernia with a round cauterization according to its quantity: and let what is touched be one-third of it. Then treat it, with what we have said: and do not add to it.
And now some of the first ones have said: that a hernia should be cauterized with a triangular cauterization, according to this form.
After it is marked with encaustic, and a line is placed which is along the width on the upper side of the hernia, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with a clave-shaped cauterization.
But the first cauterization is easier and better.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in pains due to a fall or blow.
Chapter 48.
When pain occurs in certain members due to a fall or blow, and the pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize with a punctured cauterization.
And let the cauterization of each member be according to its magnitude, and its own smallness, and its weakness, and its own strength, and the location of the twisting, and the pain from it.
If therefore he is healed by the first cauterization, it is good. If not, then apply a cautery upon it.
Since it is customary to transfer these pains from the affected member to that which approaches it. Therefore it is necessary to follow them with a cautery until the afflicted part is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in leprosy.
But lepers are sometimes helped by a cautery with the greatest benefit. And especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy; therefore, when you want to cauterize it, consider its nature.
If the leprosy is incurable and you have treated it with what we mentioned in the division, and it does not recede, nor does it stand still: and it spreads over the whole complexion of the patient: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one on the middle of the head at the crown, and a second below that towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And finally, apply your hand with the cautery for a short time, until it impresses a small impression on the mouth, and the cortices are dislocated from it: so that the expiration of gross vapors is alleviated from it, and cauterize also over the spleen itself, according to what has preceded.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the patient and appears manifestly, then it is necessary to cauterize with those cauteries which we mentioned on the head, and with a cautery on the extremity of the nose, and two cauteries on the two jaws, and two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one at the base of the tail and one above it, in that very place; and two on the hip: namely, one on each hip, and two on the knees: one on each knee, and two on the elbows, and two on the cubits, and two on the tenderness of his chest: and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of his fingers and toes; and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and on the metacarpals of his hands.
And be cautious of the nerves that are above the heel bone, so you do not injure them.
And when a branding iron is applied to the bone of the pubic area, and another to the bone of the stomach, and another to the liver.
And know that the more you add branding iron, it is the greater harm, and the more it causes damage.
And know that the weak person does not feel pain from branding iron, as the healthy ones do: therefore, because their body is already numb.
And it is necessary that the branding irons be of a magnitude, and smaller according to the members and joints: according to what precedes from the species of iron instruments.
Then treat the branding iron with flour of herbs mixed with honey, and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of branding in numbness.
When a limb is numb and is treated with medicines, and oils, and poultices, and it does not heal, then brand the numbed limb with branding irons, according to what the magnitude of the limb deserves, or its smallness.
And let your branding iron be slightly more penetrating into the thickness of the skin. Then treat it with an ointment, until it is healed.
And when branding is applied to a certain numbness that occurs in the hand or foot, in the vertebrae of the back near the exit of the nerves, which move that limb: and the numbness is removed.
But it does not work on that, unless one is skilled in the anatomy of limbs and the exit of moving nerves from the body.
Chapter 51.
When a wound is old and does not respond to any treatment from the ingenuity of medicine: then brand on it with a deep branding iron, according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed.
Then treat it with the flour of a herb, and with lentils with rose oil, and with leaves of arnoglossa, and with pigeon's blood, and with hyrundine's blood: one part from each: mix all these, and spread on a cloth, and adhere to the place until it heals.
About the method of cauterizing in Cancer.
When the cancer is beginning and you wish to restrain it: then cauterize it with a circular cauterization around its circumference, as it revolves.
The wise men have said that it should be cauterized with the final cauterization in the middle.
But it does not seem to me: because I fear that it would become an ulcer; and I have already seen that many times.
And it is better to cauterize around its circumference with a circle, as we said; or with multiple cauterizations.
About the method of cauterizing in Ulceration.
When someone has an ulceration and it is delayed in maturation, either because of the excess matter that produces it, or because of the age of the weak patient, when there is a lack of blood, or because of the time, and you wish to hasten the maturation of the ulceration, then cauterize around its circumference with many small points, puncturing with multiple cauterizations. Then let it be. For it will hasten the maturation itself.
If you wish to make a perforation of it with a cauterization, then ignite the fire of the cauterization, whose form is this.
