Chapter 61.
On the extraction of a stone in women.
A stone is rarely generated in women.
But if it happens to any of them that a stone forms, then the treatment is difficult and is prohibited because of many methods.
One of their kinds is: since a woman perhaps is a virgin.
And the second reason is that you do not find a woman who reveals herself to a doctor, when she is chaste, or among those having husbands.
The third is, because you will not find a woman who knows this art well, especially the operation with the hand.
And the fourth is remoteness from the location of the stone: therefore it requires a deep incision, and there is fear in that.
What if necessity provokes to that, then it is necessary to take a female doctor, well skilled: and she is hardly found.
If you do indeed have those things, then seek a chaste doctor, subtle and present a well-taught female obstetrician in women's matters, or a woman who has gained part of the art in this skill: make her present, and especially entrust it to her, that she may do all that you prescribe to her from the inquiry about the stone.
Firstly, it is necessary that she examine if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary that she inserts her finger into her anus, and seeks the stone.
If she has found it, she grasps it under her finger, and then instructs the midwife to insert her finger into the vagina of the woman, and inquires about the stone, after placing her left hand on the bladder, and presses with a good compression.
If she has found the stone, then it is necessary that she gradually moves it from the opening of the bladder to the lower parts with all her strength, until she reaches it at the root of the hip.
Then she presses upon it at the opposition of the middle of the vagina at the root of the hip, from whichever part it is prepared for her, and she feels the stone in that part: and her finger does not move away from the stone, grasping under it: and let there be a small incision first. Then she inserts a scalpel above that incision.
Then she inserts a scalpel above that incision. If she has felt the stone, then she adds to the second incision a quantity proportional to what the stone emerges from it.
And you should know that there are many types of stones. For it is small and large, smooth and rough, long and round with branching [veins].
Know therefore its types, so that it may be signified to you through this above what you have seen.
If therefore the blood overcomes you, then add to the place of the wound a powdered remedy, and hold it for one hour, until the blood is stanched.
Then return to your operation, until the stone comes out: and prepare yourself with the instruments that I mentioned in the extraction of stones from the veins, so that you may be assisted by them in your operation.
What if the flow of blood overcomes you, and you know that the expulsion of blood is from the artery which has been cut: then put a powder on the place, and tie it with a suitable stricture of bandages: and do not move it: and leave the stone, and do not extract it. Perhaps indeed the weak woman will die. Then treat the wound.
When therefore the acuteness of the blood has settled after some days, and the place has become putrid, then return to your operation, until the stone comes out.
Chapter 62.
On the surgical removal of a hernia in a watery place.
A watery hernia is not, unless it is an aggregation of humidity in the white membrane which is beneath the skin of the testicle containing a egg: and it is named a hernia.
And sometimes it is in its own proper membrane, which nature has prepared for it in the part of the egg, until it is felt: which is another egg, and it is the skin of the testicle between the white hernia, which we mentioned: and this does not happen unless rarely.
And the generation of this hernia is indeed from the weakness that occurs in the testicles: therefore this matter flows out to them. And when it happens from a blow above the testicles.
And this humidity is having many colors. Or indeed its color is declining to yellowish, or it is bloody red, or foul, black, or it is watery white, and it is that which is in excess.
And the signs by which it is known where the accumulation of water is, are these. For if it is in the white skin that we mentioned, then the abscess is round in length for a short time, like an egg figure; and the testicle does not appear, since the humidity surrounds it on all sides.
And if there is humidity in its own skin fold, then the abscess is round with an egg-like part, and for this reason a man thinks it is another egg.
And if the humidity is between the skin of the testicles and the white skin, then it falls under the sense.
When therefore you make a cognitive effort concerning the color of humidity, then experience the color of humidity in the abscess with an inserted quadrilateral, whose form precedes. According to that which emerges in the investigation of the inserted quadrilateral, judge concerning that which is between itself.
When therefore we come to the treatment with iron, then it is necessary that you should caution the weak, so that they may be bled if possible, and you will see their body full.
Then let it rest on its back on a high place, and put many cloths under it.
Then sit on its left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on its right side, who should stretch out his arm to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles, and towards the wondrous part of the belly.
Then take a broad spatula, and separate the skin of the testicles from the middle along the length, up to the perineum; and make an incision according to the straightness of the equidistant line that divides the skin of the testicles, until you reach the white skin that surrounds it; and scrape it off and observe, or be cautious about this, so that you may separate it: and your scraping should be such as you scrape it off, from the part that is suspended with an egg more; and scrutinize subtly with the scraping according to the quantity that is possible for you.
Then pierce a full water-perforating siphac with a broad perforation, and extract all the water.
Then separate the two labia of the section with hooks, and extend the siphac to the superior areas, and do not touch the skin covering the testicles: and make an incision in the siphac however it is possible for you to make the incision, either totally or partially, especially on its subtle side. For if you do not carefully examine it, there will be no security in the incision, lest the water returns.
If however the matter proceeds outward from its skin during the time of your operation: then when you have completed the section of the siphac, reduce it. Then bring together the two labia of the skin of the testicles with a suture.
Then treat it as you would other wounds, until it heals.
If you find a corrupted matter from the blackness of another, then it is necessary to bind the vessels, which are the suspenders, fearing the flow of blood.
Then cut off the testicle with its suspender, and extract the matter: afterwards treat it as we have said.
If water has collected in two parts, then know that there are two branches: therefore dry up the other part equally, according to what you did in the other.
And if it is equal to you, so that there may be one operation, then do it: afterwards stop the bleeding. And introduce into the sections a wool soaked in oil, or in rose oil: and place before a wool which you have soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over both testicles, and soften the belly: and place above double cloths, and they are poultices: and bind them above with a ligature, which has six threads according to this form.
Then two cloths are applied, and they are soaked, and filled with a warming powder, according to this likeness: and let the extremities be pressed with a hot cloth or damp wool: and they are gathered together with a binding in the loin of the arms: and one extremity receives above the anus up to the back, and the second receives towards the pubic area: and two extremities above the two hips below, and two other extremities above the two groin areas, and all are gathered together with a binding in the loin of the arms.
And when you treat this ramex artificially with a cautery at the site of the section with iron; and it is, as if you were to receive a subtle cautery instrument, and cut through the skin of the testicles: and it is ignited, according to what we have narrated: until when it is detected that the white album containing water appears: then take the cautery, according to this method.
The Greek letters are assimilated.
Then pierce with it that album, and it is ignited, until all the moisture emerges.
Then stretch out the album with hooks, and scrape it with a subtle, ignited cautery, and cut into it as much as possible for you, until you eradicate all of it.
And beware lest you touch it with fire.
And know that this operation is more beneficial and farther from the flow of blood, and better than an operation with a section.
If however it causes a contrary effect in the hour of section, or in the hour of cautery, or apostema warm, or flow of blood, or something else: then it is necessary to cure what causes a contrary effect for you from that with the treatment which suits it, according to what has been mentioned.
If however the patient is faint-hearted and does not expect to survive this operation, due to its own horror: then administer the piercing according to what I have narrated; and it is.
When it is certified to you, through what we have said about the signs, that the ramex is watery: then it is necessary for you to make the patient sit on an elevated seat.
Then pierce the apostema in its lower part with a broad spatula: and put the piercing according to the length of the body, and let the opening be wide, until all the water flows out.
Then put it on a cotton pad, and bind it, and leave it until the remaining water flows out: then treat it, until the wound is healed.
If however the contrary happens with the flow of water at the time when it perforates it, and it does not happen unless for this reason, because a white membrane creates a contrary flow in the orifice of the wound, and prohibits the exit of water: then it is necessary to introduce a feather into the wound, or an instrument by which the hydropic water is extracted, whose form has been mentioned beforehand; or add in the operation of the wound for a short time.
And know that the water returns and accumulates after six months, or around them. When therefore it accumulates, then it is treated according to the same method, and it passes through its own weak days.
Chapter 63.
On the treatment of fleshy wounds.
Know that in the incision above this wound, it is from a fear of causing harm in many dispositions. Wherefore it seems to me that its dismissal is to be saved from those things.
And I am mindful of the operation on it, and the type of abscess.
I say therefore that many abscesses occur in the bodies, from which the swellings are composed: and it happens for many causes, namely.
Or from acute or sharp superfluities which flow out to the swellings. Or from blows.
And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body, and no pain is found in it: and it is a grave abscess.
And perhaps it is a stony abscess, whose color is dark, and there is no sensation in it.
And when it happens from the nodulation of arteries, and their inflammation: as I have already mentioned its remembrance: or from the inflammation of veins.
Which therefore is from them due to the inflammation of arteries, is recognized by the arrangement of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers. And it is not suitable that you touch it immediately.
That which occurs from the swelling of veins is not dispersed by pressure with the fingers.
And now it is possible that a section is made on this species, and on the remaining flesh; and it is to cut through the skin of the testicles. Then stretch the egg upwards, and extract it with a white cloth: and free the suspensory ligament from the vessels, and tie the vessels: and cut the suspensory ligament after you have freed it on all sides from the parts of the egg.
If therefore the egg is consolidated with those naturally born flesh, then it is suitable that you should pull out the egg, and cut into it.
And if there is an adhesion between something from the sipakhah, or in what is between the vessels: then it is suitable that you free the entire adhesion, and cut into it with a rounded incision.
If, however, there is a nativity of flesh at the place of adhesion which is behind: then it is suitable that you cut through the whole of it, and extract the egg, as we have said.
When therefore your operation is complete, then fill the wound with a piece of cloth soaked in rose oil and wine: thereafter treat it with the remaining treatment, until it heals.
Chapter 63.
Concerning the treatment of Varicose veins, which is with a Vein.
Ulcer is a hidden aposteme, which is an inward gathering, similar to a swelling, with softening of the testicles: and it becomes difficult upon weak movement and exercise, and walking.
And in the treatment of this disease is from fear, because of that which precedes, namely remembrance.
But it is necessary that we describe the operation on it according to what the first ones did.
I say therefore, that it is suitable for you to make the weak person sit on a raised seat. Then apply the supporting bandage to the lower testicles. Then hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, along with the nearby veins: and let another assistant hold them in place with a vigorous extension.
Then make an incision with a broad, sharp scalpel in a crosswise section directly on the veins, until they are exposed.
Then scrape away from every part, as we have instructed you in the extraction of the Arteries that are in the temples.
Next, place a thread in them where there is a double filament, and tie it at the first places to which the veins are attached: and tie it again at their ends. Then cut them off in a straight section in the middle, according to the length of the body, and extract what is gathered from the foul, corrupted humors.
Then treat the wound with the treatment of other wounds, in which it is customary to generate a healthy scab, so that the veins that nourish one of the testicles may fall away. For it is not an evil through that.
But if all the veins are affected, then it is necessary to extract the testicles along with their veins: so that they may not be deprived of nourishment, and wither away, or become putrid, and may not be a source of trouble with them.
Chapter 65.
On the treatment of an intestinal hernia.
The cause of this hernia is from a rupture, which occurs in the extended suture above the navel on the inguinal part of the belly.
Because the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles. And this rupture is either from the suture or its extension.
And these two types occur from many causes: either from a blow, or a fall, or a shout, or the lifting of a heavy object, and similar things.
And the symptom, when it is from an extension of a sifach. It is what happens gradually over a long period of time and does not happen suddenly; and it is an equal aposteme compared to a deep one; therefore, because the sifach compresses the intestine.
And the symptom of it is when it is from a section of sifach, because it causes to happen from the beginning of its vehement sudden pain; and it is a diverse aposteme, appearing near the skin surface; and that is on account of the exit of the intestine, and its course to the exterior of the sifach.
And when it goes out with the intestine a zirb; and it is called this Ramex intestinalis, and zirbia; and when it happens with flatulence.
And when it flows into the intestine with feces, and is retained there; and it is with that a most grievous affliction of the infirm; because it causes to happen a bad pain, and especially when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of this type of illness with iron, there is fear; therefore it is necessary to be cautious in that case.
And the method of operation is, to press on the infirm person, so that they reduce their intestine with their own hand to the internal concavity, if it obeys and returns. Then it is supported above its neck between your hands; and elevate its knees.
Then stretch the skin that follows the skin to the upper parts, and separate the entire skin of the testicles along its length. Then place on both lips of the section a curved needle, according to what is necessary to open the section with them; and let the section be according to quantity, as much as is possible, so that an egg can come out from it.
Then remove the skin, and what is beneath the skin of the testicles, until when the white sifach is discovered, hard on every side; then introduce your index finger into that which follows the testicle, into that which is between the white siphach, which is beneath the skin of the egg, and between the sifach secondly, and separate it completely from the adhesion which is in the posterior part of the egg.
Then place the right hand inside the scrotum to support the testicles; and with this hand, extend the suture upwards, with the left hand; and elevate the opening with the suture to the part of the section; and order the assistant to extend the opening upwards; and you will release the adhesion which is behind the complete solution.
And search with your fingers, so that there may not be something hidden from the intestine in the hard white suture. If you find something from it: then push it down to the lower abdomen.
Then take a needle, in which there is a thick thread, made into a licinium of ten threads; and insert it at the back of the suture, that is, the sheath, which is under the skin of the testicles following the section; then cut the ends that emerge from the thread, until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them over others in the shape of a cross; and tie with those sutures, which we mentioned earlier, because it is under the skin of the testicles with a strong ligament, until nothing can pass through, which nourishes them, to send something to them: so that hot aposteme does not occur there. And place the second ligature outside the first ligature, at a distance of less than two fingers from it. And after these two ligatures, leave the suture that is under the skin of the testicles a quantity equal to the size of a finger; and cut the remaining whole part according to its roundness, and remove the opening from it.
Then cauterize the lower part of the incision of the testicles, from which blood and serum flow, as we have narrated in what has been mentioned before.
Then apply a soft cotton pad soaked in oil, and put it on the wound; and apply the ligature that we have narrated. And when you cauterize the white suture that we mentioned, after the incision, fearing a flow of blood. For it often happens that. And release the bandage, until it falls off by itself.
If, however, its fall is delayed, then it should be soaked with warm water; and place on top of it what we mentioned earlier, until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with the remaining treatment for wounds, until it is cured.
Chapter 66.
Concerning the windy vein.
In this windy vein, I have not seen anyone who has dared to attempt its cure with an iron instrument.
And the first ones indeed said that it should be done as we described in the windy vein that is with a splint. Which is to bind the splints above it with a facilitating bandage: then sew in the middle, and treat afterwards with what opens it, until the splints fall off: and treat the wound, according to what we said, until it is healed.
Chapter 67.
Concerning the rupture that occurs in the groin.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, as we said, and the place protrudes, but nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles: and if it does descend, it is small, and returns at all hours: truly, if it is prolonged with that time, a fissure is added in the perineum, until the intestines descend into the perineum.
And it happens from the extension of the perineum, which is in the groin, as we said. Which is because the perineum is extended: then it becomes soft and putrid, and the place protrudes.
And its treatment is with a cautery, as its previous narrative has mentioned.
And sometimes it is treated with an iron instrument, in this manner: and it is, as if the weak one lies on his back between your hands. Then sew the place of the putrid and protruding rupture, making an incision across its width, according to the size of three fingers.
Then you should stitch alsifak and those that are under the skin, until when it is touched, a white album appears, which is under the skin and follows it.
Then take a scalpel, and place it on the prominent area of the alsifak, and press it deeply into the wound.
Then you should have two prominent areas on the extremity of the radius from the alsifak, and connect one of them with a suture to the other; then withdraw the extremity of the radius.
And do not cut the entire alsifak, nor stretch a vein, nor anything else, just as I taught you to know in the treatment of an intestinal obstruction.
Then take care of that wound's treatment. When you have made the incision, clean it, and restore the wound, until it becomes consolidated.
For it is constricted, and not adding to the prominence of the Rupture.
And cauterization is better in this place: because it is closer to health.
Chapter 68.
On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
The skin of the testicles often becomes soft in certain men, because the flesh that is between them becomes softened and their appearance becomes foul.
Therefore it is necessary for the one who is seeking treatment for this condition to make the weak part rest on its back, and to incise the entire softened skin over the natural skin.
Then bring together the two lips with a suture: and if you wish, you should first remove the excess of softened skin with three sutures, or four, and make a firm suture.
Then incise between the sutures.
Then take care of the treatment of the remaining wounds, until they heal, and the threads fall out.
Chapter 69.
On Castration.
You should know that Castration is forbidden by our law: and because of this it was permitted to me not to mention it in my book: and there is no need for a mention of it, unless for two reasons.
One of them is that it should be in the knowledge of a physician when he is questioned about it, and so that he knows the treatment for which it occurs.
And another method is that we often need to castrate certain animals because of our injuries through them, such asrams, goats, and cats, and similar ones from animals.
Therefore, I say that Castration is done according to two methods. Or by subtraction. Or by incision and cutting.
In that one which is done by subtraction, the method of operation is this: we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles become soft and relaxed, and hang down; then you rub them with your hand until they dissolve and do not appear to the touch.
In castration by incision and cutting, it is necessary to hold the animal, and press down on the cord of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensor, and cut above each one with a single section, until two testicles proceed: then incise after you have removed both, and do not leave anything on them except a subtle sifa, which is above the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than the one done by subtraction: because subtraction perhaps leaves something in the testicles, for which reason the animal desires mating.
Then treat the wound, until it heals.
Chapter 70.
 On the treatment of Hermaphrodites of two modes.
A Hermaphrodite is treated from the urine in two modes. One of them is because it appears in the following space, or in the hollow of the testicles, in what is between the two testicles, a figure like a woman's vulva, in which there are hairs; and sometimes urine flows out from what is in the hollow of the testicles.
In women, there is one species, and it is the vulva of a woman situated above the pubic bone, like small testicles of a man, protruding externally; of which one is like the penis of a man, and two are like two testicles.
And the treatment of these three species, two from men and one from women, is: because it is necessary to cut away the added flesh, until their impression is eliminated. Then heal them with the healing of remaining wounds.
In the second species of men, from which urine exits, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment at all.
Chapter 71.
On the Incision of the Tentigen and the Eminent Flesh in the Vulvae of Women.
The Tentigen is perhaps added above the natural thing, until it becomes disgusting and its appearance is repulsive; and sometimes it grows so much in some women that it expands like in men, and reaches all the way to sexual intercourse.
It is necessary therefore to hold back the excess of the Tentigen with your hand or with a hook, and to cut it away; and not to stop in the incision, especially in the deep root: so that there may not be a flow of blood.
Then heal the wound itself with treatment, until it is healed.
A carnosity arises, which is born in the orifice of the womb, until it fills it; and perhaps it protrudes externally resembling a tail; and because of that some people call it a "tail-like" disease. It is necessary therefore to cut away the carnosity as we cut away the Tentigen, and to treat it, until it is healed.
On the treatment of the Alratica, which is a woman's vulva not pierced.
Chapter 72.
The Alratica is when the vulva of a woman is not pierced, or has a small opening. It is either natural or accidental.
It is accidental, resulting from an illness that preceded it; and indeed it occurs either from flesh born with it, or from subtle thinness, or from being compact; and it happens either in the depths of the womb, or in its sides, or at the top or bottom of it; and it prevents coitus and impregnation, and childbirth, and perhaps prevents menstruation.
And the recognition of it is by the obstetrician's observation, if the obstruction is apparently close at hand.
If, however, it is not apparent, then you should examine it with your fingers, or with a rod.
If, however, the obstruction is from subtle thinness and is close to the two lips: then you should probe and dissect it.
And it is, as you place above the two labial mounds.
Then place your index fingers of both hands simultaneously, and let the woman sit on her back with her knees spread apart. Then stretch out the two lips with force, until the subtle thinness is dissected and the obstruction is opened up.
Then take a piece of wool, and soak it in oil, and place it on the location; and let the woman apply it every day, so that the area does not consolidate into another scar.
If, however, the thinness is thick and compact: then it is necessary to cut it with a broad spatula-like instrument similar to a myrtle leaf.
If, however, the obstruction is from flesh born with it, then suspend it with hooks, and incise it: and let there be with you medicines that suppress the flux of blood without biting, such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and thus aggregated with white albumen.
Then administer a cannula made of broad lead, so that the wound does not consolidate quickly, hold it for some days: and administer a dry linen dressing, then proceed with the remaining treatment, until it is healed.
And when a swelling appears in the matrix of a born flesh wound: it is necessary therefore to make an incision according to this method: since there is no cancerous abscess, for it does not become contrary with iron at all.
Chapter 73.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, Athelil, and the red swelling on the vulva of women.
Hemorrhoids are indeed the openings of the veins, from which much blood flows out continuously.
Since hemorrhoids are old and established, they become thelil; and I have already spoken about the division of their types and signs in the same chapter, and I will say here which ones receive a cure and which ones do not.
I say therefore that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the womb and do not appear to the senses, then there is no cure for them with iron.
But those which are in the opening of the womb and are perceived by the senses, are those that can be cured.
It is necessary therefore to introduce the woman into a cold house. Then extend Athelil with forceps, or with a rough cloth, and cut them out from their roots.
Then powder over them against the flow of blood from one powder of incisions without causing harm: such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and frankincense, and similar things.
Then apply her feet to the wall for an hour. Afterwards, put her in cold water.
If the flow of blood has persisted: then make her sit in a decoction of sumach, and cortex of granates, and gall, and similar things.
Then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it over her back.
If therefore the blood is staunched with it, it is good: and if not, apply cups to her back and breasts without making incisions.
Then take a linen cloth and dip it into the juice of tarantula, or the juice of wild pomegranate, or the juice of leaves of aloe, that is to say, of galangal, with a certain Pontic wine, and make it adhere to the place.
When therefore the aposteme subsides, then treat the place with ointments, until it is healed.
The Albarth ulcer is similar to a red pustule on the heads of alhaz, and its appearance is rough.
It is necessary therefore that you cut what appears from it, according to what I said about the lil equalizing: and treat it, until it is healed.
Chapter 83.
Concerning the perforation of the uterus which occurs in the womb.
There occur in the womb many species of apostemes, such as cancer, and stone-like aposteme, and ulcers, and adubelations, and alekilations, that is to say, herpes, aestiomemus, and fistulae, and hemorrhoids, and ragadiae, and thelil, and hot aposteme.
And I have already said all these diseases and their species, and their signs, and their cures in the division: it is necessary that I speak about the hot aposteme which occurs in the womb, when it arises from the apostemes that collect blood, and you should know how to perform its opening with an iron instrument.
It is necessary therefore that you consider. Then if the pain of the aposteme in its incision is acute with percussion and flame and fever: and you see it red: if sense falls upon it, then do not press with its perforation: and treat it with that which helps above maturation, until when the acute accidents subside.
Then it is necessary that you make the woman sit on a seat which has two footstools, and recline or lie on her back, and join her feet to the lower part of the belly: and let her hips be expanded, and place her arms under her thighs, and bind them with a convenient ligature to that.
Then the obstetrician sits on the right side and administers an instrument by which the opening of the womb is revealed.
And it is necessary when you administer this instrument, to fix it with the deep root of the woman's womb: so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the womb, and harms the weak woman.
But if the instrument is more than the depth, then it is necessary to place pads on the covering of the deep womb: so that the entrance of the entire instrument into the depth of the womb is prohibited: and it is necessary to place a curl, which runs in the instrument, from the upper side: and to hold the instrument, and to revolve the minister's curl, until the depth of the womb is revealed.
When therefore the exit appears, and is touched by hand, and it is gentle and soft: then it is necessary to separate it at its head with a spatula.
When therefore the blood is evacuated, then it is necessary to place the wounded lip submerged in rose oil: or green oil, in which there is some astringency: and place the lip, and extract the section from the depth of the womb.
And place it outside on the womb, and on the pubic area a clean woolen cloth submerged in water, in which there are boiled mallow roots.
Then it should be treated after two days with an ointment that is suitable for that, until it heals.
And when the womb and wound are washed, so that it is cleaned with water and honey: then with water in which the root of lily or long aristolochia has been boiled: then return to the ointment.
What if the wound was hidden inside the womb, then it is necessary to refrain from curing it with iron, rather cure it with what we said in the division.
Chapter 70.
The teachings on obstetrics, how they treat embryos that have emerged in a shape not natural.
It is necessary for the obstetrician to recognize first the shape of a naturally formed fetus.
From these signs, therefore, it is clear that when you see a woman pressed down to the lower parts, and she desires to smell the air, and becomes relieved over what is on her from the fetus, and hastens the exit of the embryo: then know that this fetus is according to its natural shape, and its exit is through its own head, and the afterbirth with it: or hanging, or suspended from the navel.
When you see these signs, then it is necessary that her womb be compressed, so that the embryo may come down quickly.
For when it comes down through its own head, the afterbirth comes down with it, and is cleansed of those excessive impurities by a good cleansing.
But one that is beyond this fetus is unnatural, inadvisable.
Because sometimes the fetus comes out on its feet, and its body comes out before its head, and one of its hands or one of its feet: or its head and one of its hands come out: or its belly comes out: and perhaps it turns over onto its neck, and similar things from unnatural shapes.
It is necessary therefore for the obstetrician to be prudent and subtle in all these things, and to beware of error and deception: and I am showing every shape from them, and how the ingenuity is in it, and is signified by that, and stands upon it.
When the fetus comes out through its own natural exit, and it is difficult for the woman, and the childbirth is hard for her, and you see that her strength is already debilitated: then make her sit on a chair, or let other women hold her: and apply warm vapors to her womb with decoction of fenugreek, and with humid olive oil.
Then the midwife inserts a small spatula between her fingers and finds the second one with it, and separates it from her nail, until she feels what is in it from the moisture: and presses on the woman's abdomen, until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then it is necessary that the woman be anointed with a clyster of fenugreek, with sesame oil.
Then advise her to compress herself after the clyster, and make her sneeze with the conditions, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour. For the fetus will come out immediately.
If two hands of the fetus come out first, then it is necessary to reduce them with gentle facilitation little by little. If it does not obey at the entrance, then put the woman on a chair, and elevate her feet upwards; then strike the chair on the ground; and let the woman be held, so that she does not fall at the shock.
If therefore the hands do not come out, and the fetus dies: then cut them, and extract the remaining part of the fetus: and bind her hand with a cloth, and extract it with equality: for it itself will come out.
The extraction of the embryo from its feet. When the fetus comes out onto its feet, then it is necessary to push them upwards; afterwards, convert the fetus little by little; subsequently, straighten it.
Then take one of its feet and extend it little by little.
When they come out as far as the hips, then advise her to compress herself, and make her sneeze with the conditions; for it will come out, if God wishes.
And if it does not come out with what we have narrated, then reduce the fetus little by little, until you place it according to its natural figure. For it itself will come out then with an easy delivery.
If it is prohibited with all that we have narrated: then take from the mucilage of the altea, and oil of sisamin, and dissolved gum: and strike everything in a mortar with good percussion. Then apply it to the wound of the woman's vulva, and beneath her belly. Then have her sit in warm water, until she feels the hypochondrium.
When you see that the lower parts are already warmed up, then have her receive a suffumigation of myrrh: and apply it. When she holds the suffumigation for one hour, then have her sit on a seat. Then have her sniff it out: and clear her nose and mouth: and press the lower part of the belly with easy compression. For the fetus will come out immediately.
The delivery of the fetus on knees and hands. When it comes out according to this method, then she should introduce her hands little by little. Then the woman should be raised to her neck, and her feet should hang down below: and she herself should sit on a bed, and fold her hands. Then press above her belly little by little. Then extract what is under her feet from the pillows, until it is prepared in the lower part. If the fetus does not come out, then take her feet and move them with a vigorous motion. Then press what is above the hypochondrium little by little, until the fetus ascends to the upper parts. Then introduce her hands and adjust the fetus little by little: and instruct the woman to press, until the fetus comes out.
The delivery of the fetus, hanging sideways from the hands. It is introduced in the reduction of her hands. If she cannot reduce it, then raise the woman up, and have her walk around.
If indeed he cannot walk, then make him lie on a bed and shake his hips with a vigorous concussion.
Then administer the liniment you prepared from mucilages.
What if he receives that potion, then make him sit on a seat. Then study the reduction of the hand, and equalize the foetus according to the natural figure: and make the woman sneeze, and order her to compress herself until it comes out.
The exit of the foetus is over its neck, with hands extended, and its face is towards the back of its mother. It is necessary that the midwife holds the hand of the foetus, then turns it around slowly, and adjusts it with ease.
When it is adjusted, then put on its belly what we have prepared from oil and mucilages.
Then order her to move slowly. When you have done that, then make her sit on a seat, and order her to lean towards the right side. Then order her to compress herself: and make her sneeze with a condition.
The exit of the prepared foetus is on its side. When it descends to the maternal orifice in this manner with the afterbirth, then separate the afterbirth with your finger, until it is evacuated from the moisture.
If it is suspended over the face of the foetus and its neck, then cut it from the navel: so that it is not retained, and does not die.
Then push the foetus towards the interior, until you place it according to what is proper: and order the woman to compress herself several times: for indeed it will come out with a gentle exit.
The exit of twins, or many foetuses. You know that twins are often born: and sometimes three, and four. However, that external thing is rare and rarely happens.
There are five things beyond nature, and they do not penetrate deeply; and they bind them, however much they multiply, with a secondary one; and they are separated by a suture, distinguishing between them the tied part in each of their navels.
And when they emerge, just as one fetus emerges by a natural outlet, easily; and they emerge by an unnatural outlet, as we have narrated.
If they are difficult when some of them are at the part, and they reach that which we said from unnatural figures, then treat them as we have narrated; and let there be a subtle and precise treatment, and let it do what it does with facility and slowness, and let it be adapted according to every figure with what is prepared for it by a leading ingenuity for health.
The reminder of that which is formed in the womb from embryos and are aborted.
When one is formed in the womb, and two, and three, and four, and five, and six, and seven, and more than ten; and it has already been verified by me, that a woman aborting has expelled seven, and another fifteen, all fully formed.
That which was done by the measurement of the glorious wise one.
Therefore, this whole thing is necessary for it to be in the science of Obstetrics. Perhaps indeed it will reach that similar thing: therefore let it be opposed to it with what is fitting.
Chapter 76.
On the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with what I said in the division from medication, and it does not emerge, and you are forced to use manual operation, then it is necessary to consider.
If the woman is of healthy virtue, and she does not have any of the accidents from which loss is feared on her behalf: then it is necessary for the woman to be placed on a bed, on her back, with her head inclined downwards, and her thighs elevated; and an assistant should hold her from both sides, or bind her to the bed, so that her body does not move during the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the wound of the matrix with humid oils, along with mucus from the flax plant, and fenugreek, and linseed.
Then anoint the midwife's hand with these oils and mucus; then insert it into the womb with ease. Then feel with it the place where the fetus is stuck, and find a convenient position for that.
Consider therefore then, if the fetus is prepared to descend onto its own head: then fix hooks in its eyes, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or on its palate, or under its beard, or in its armpits, and near its ribs, and under its hip bones.
But if the descent is onto its feet, then in its pubic area, and its middle ribs.
And it is necessary to hold the hook with the right hand, and place its curvature in what is between the fingers of the left hand: and insert it with ease, and fix the hook in one of those places that we mentioned, until it reaches the empty space.
Then fix another hook opposite it, or a third if necessary: so that there is equal traction, and it does not lean to one side.
Then it is extended with equal extension, and not only stretched in a straight line, but rather moved to every side, so that the outcome of its extraction may be alleviated: just as it is done with a tooth during its removal.
And it is necessary in what is between them, to soften the extension. If a part of it is retained, then it is necessary for the midwife to anoint certain fingers with oil and insert them from one side, so that she may revolve what is retained with them.
If a part of the fetus emerges, then the hooks are changed to another place that is higher: do this until the entire fetus emerges.
If therefore the hand protrudes before the others, and it is not possible to reduce it, on account of its contraction: then it is necessary to wrap a bandage around it. Then extract it thus when it protrudes entirely, either by cutting into the joint of the sole or in the elbow; and thus it is necessary to do likewise on the other hand, and on both feet.
If however the head of the fetus is large, or there happens to be a contraction at the outlet, or there is water accumulated in its head: then it is necessary to introduce between the fingers a spatula with a pointed end, and to find the head with it, and to extract the water: or to dislodge it with an instrument called Almisdac, whose form comes with the forms of other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
Likewise, if the fetus is of a large-headed nature, then it is necessary to sever the shoulder joint; or to extract it with a misdach, as we have said. Then hook out the bones with forceps.
What if the head protrudes and is constricted at the waist: then it is necessary to feel around until the moisture that is in the chest is discharged.
If however it does not progress and does not come out at the outlet: then cut the head a little, according to what is possible for you.
What if the lower part of the abdomen is inflamed, or there is dropsy in it: then it is necessary to perforate it, until the moisture flows out from it.
If however the fetus is on its feet, then its extraction is easy, and its direction towards the womb's mouth is light.
If however it is constricted at the abdomen or chest: then it is necessary to extract it with a cloth that you have wrapped around your hand; and feel the abdomen or chest, until what is in them flows out.
If however the remaining limbs are exhausted and the head returns: then the Obstetrician inserts their left hand. If therefore the womb is open, then they insert their hand deeply into the womb and feel with it the head, and draw it out with their fingers up to the mouth of the womb: then they insert one hook or two hooks, and draw it out with them.
If the womb is constricted, because of the warm apostema that has happened to it: then it is not fitting to struggle over it, but rather to administer an effusion of humid and greasy things, and apply an emollient plaster: and sit in waters that soften and moisten.
If the fetus is on its side, then it is possible to straighten it: then administer what we said regarding the living fetus.
If it is not possible, then it should be dissected piece by piece and extracted.
And it is necessary that you do not leave anything of the secondine inside at all.
When you have completed your operation, then administer what we said regarding the warm apostemas that occur in the wombs.
If a flow of blood occurs, then sit in astringent waters and administer the remaining treatment.
And I have indeed already seen a woman, in whose womb a dead fetus was: then she became pregnant again with another, afterwards that other fetus also died. So it happened to her after a long time an apostema in her navel, and it became swollen, until it opened: and began to discharge pus.
I was therefore called to her treatment, and I treated her for a long time: but the wound did not heal.
I then applied to it certain strong attractive plasters: and it came out from its place, the bone. Then several days passed, and another bone came out. I was amazed therefore, since there is no bone in the belly.
I thought therefore that they were from the bones of a dead fetus.
I examined the wound, and I extracted many bones, while the woman was in her best dispositions: and already she had lived a long time, and a little pus came out from the place.
And I did not confirm this external thing, unless there is science in it, and help for that which the skilled physician administers with his hand from the healing.
Chapter 77.
On the forms of necessary instruments for extracting a fetus.
The form of the Forceps which opens the womb.
Here is described the form of the Forceps, which are equalized to books, which have two equal arms at the extremities of two wooden handles. However, this vertigo ought to be more subtle than the forceps: and that it may be so, whether made from ebony or from boxwood.
And the width of all the wood is almost two fingers: and the edge of each of the two is almost one finger, and their length is a palm and a half: and in the middle of the two wooden pieces are two additions of the same kind of wood, which are already fixed to both, whose length is a half-palm plus a little: and the width of each is almost two fingers, or a little more.
And these two additions are inserted into the maternal passage, so that they open with them when you turn the two Forceps.
Another form similar to that one, more subtle and lighter.
Let it be made from ebony wood or boxwood, according to the similarity of the forceps. However, at its extremity there are two additions, as you see here above: and the length of each addition is almost a palm: and the width of each is two fingers.
When you are about to dissect a corpse with it, then make the woman sit on a couch, with her feet hanging down, opening what is between her thighs. Then insert these two connected additions into the corpse, and you holding the instrument's extremity below between her hips. Then open your hand with the instrument, just as you do with forceps, equally according to the quantity that you wish to open in the mouth of the corpse, until the midwife does what she wants.
The shape of a Turning alternative to what the ancients said, the Shape of an Expeller by which the fetus is expelled.
The shape of Almisdac, where the large head is constrained: and it is similar to forceps, which have teeth at the extremity, as you see.
And when it is made oval, like forceps according to this shape, as you see, which have teeth like serrated teeth, by which it is cut and constrained.
The shape of a Ring having one spine.
The shape of a Ring having two spines.
The shape of a Spoon-like instrument having two extremities for cutting off the head.
The shape of two Spoon-like instruments, also wider ones.
All these instruments are exercised, and the more their species are multiplied, and they are prepared by the craftsman, the swifter is their operation, and the more esteemed they are among men, due to their quantity.
Do not despise any of these instruments, as long as it is prepared by you. For the necessity of them is inexcusable.
Head 78.
 On the extraction of the Afterbirth.
When the second ligature is retained at the wound, then it is necessary to apply a compress to the weakened area, so that it may retain its breath. Then make her sternutate with concoctions; and bind your hand over her bone, and her nostrils. If therefore it goes out through this, it is good.
If not: then take a pot, and perforate it in the covering hole: and put in it herbs opening up the womb, such as marjoram, rue, and anise, and chamomile, and senna, and lignified cassia, and centaury: take all these herbs, or some of them, and submerge them with water, and put them over the fire.
Then put an embryo of a certain bush over the hole of the covering pot, and another extremity into the womb: and hold it until the vapour reaches the concavity of the womb.
Then make her sternutate, as we said. For the second ligature will go out with ease.

For it has obeyed then, and is preserved, and is freed from adherence.
If the maternal bone is constricted, as we have already narrated: treat it with sternutatio, and from medicine of the ollea with herbs.
If however it does not come out with all that we have narrated, then beware lest you weary yourself over it in the repetition of the extraction.
It is necessary, so that what comes out from the maternal bone, binds to the hip joint of the woman. Then anoint it with a tetrapharmacon ointment. For it will putrefy itself after days, and dissolve, and come out.
But when it putrefies, a bad smell rises from it to the stomach and head, and hurts that weak woman. It is necessary therefore that suitable fumigations be administered to her.
Some of the ancients have already experienced the fumigation of nasturtium and dried figs.
The form of the instrument with which the woman is fumigated at the retention of the Secondina and menses.

Chapter 79.
Concerning the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many boys are born, and their anus is not perforated, which has already been obstructed by a subtle sip of milk. It is necessary therefore that the midwife should perforate it with her finger: and if not, she should perforate it with a sharp spatula: and let her beware lest she hurts him.
Then put on it a woolen cloth infused with wine and oil. Then treat him with ointments, until he is healed.
If however it is blocked, then put a cannula of lead in the orifice for many days, and it will be digested when the boy wants to expel.
And now there occurs a blockage of the anus also from the consolidation of the wound or from an abscess. It is necessary therefore that the consolidation be cut, then treated with what we mentioned regarding treatment and lead.
Chapter 80.
Of the treatment of fistulas which occur in the lower part.
Fistulas which occur in the lower part are a swelling and a hardness which occur near the anus outwardly: or in a single part of the body: and it is one fistula, or several.
When therefore that swelling becomes old, it opens, and there flows out from it a watery white fluid, or subtle pus.
And sometimes they are penetrating fistulas from these. Therefore the penetrating ones are recognized by that which comes out from straining and flatulence, when the weak person is straining, and perhaps worms come out from them.
And they are fistulas when they are penetrating in the body up to the bladder, and up to the root of the penis. And they are penetrating ones up to the joint of the hip, and up to the knot of the tailbone.
From this it is recognized that the penetrating fistula reaches up to the anus, and also from the non-penetrating one, by inserting your index finger into the anus: and you insert a subtle probe into the fistula through a tube or iron, when there is no twisting.
If there is twisting in it, then insert into it a subtle probe of lead, or a pin from horsehair pillows, until you feel the probe, or pin on your finger.
If you do not feel it deeply, nor does anything proceed from the orifice during straining, nor flatulence, nor worms as I said: then know that it is not penetrating: therefore hasten to treatment.
And when a fistula is penetrating to the bladder or to the urinary meatus: then its indication is the outflow of urine from it, and its prohibition from this so that the place may be consolidated with medicines.
If it is penetrating to the joint of the hip, or to the mouth of the hip: then its sign is that it reaches the tendons up to that place, if there is no twisting up to the mouth: and the discovery of pain in the surrounding area, and that pus always flows out from it: and that medicine is not effective for it, nor is it consolidated with an ointment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas there is no complete cure: and the treatment of them is labor and vanity to him, by foolish doctors, who are deceived about it.
In that one, however, which is not penetrating and not chronic, healing can be hoped for with a serum: according to what I tell you, and I have already proven it: and it is so that the patient lies between your hands on his back: and lift his legs up above his hips, and his hips are inclined towards his abdomen. Then a lead or copper probe is inserted, if there is twisting in the fistula, until you know where it reaches the tendons.
If however the patient feels it around the anus, then it is necessary to insert your index finger into the anus.
If therefore you feel with your finger the tendons already penetrated by themselves detected, besides what you feel between your finger and the skin, or flesh: then therefore you know for certain that it is penetrating: so do not labor in it, because there is no healing of it, as we have said.
They have said, however, that it can be healed in certain men with flesh, and from the medication by which they hope for a benefit, it is to apply a subtle cauterizing fire according to the width of the fistula, as previously mentioned, and insert the ignited thing into the fistula, until it reaches around the anus. Then repeat that twice or three times, so that you know, because those added fleshy growths are already purified, which are similar to the quill pen of a bird.
Then treat it with liniments wrapped in butter, until those fleshy growths emerge, which are purified: then treat it with salves that generate and consolidate flesh.
If therefore it heals, it is good.
And if not, then it does not heal with any other treatment ever.
And if it emerges as a point, and has not penetrated up to your finger, which is in the anus, and there is a thick or fleshy or scabby obstacle between it and the point, or scab: and you see a Fistula in that which follows the surface of the skin, then you cut the skin from the beginning of the Fistula, and you guide the cutting with the point that is in the fistula, until the cutting reaches where the point of the fistula ends, and the point is freed and falls out.
Then cleanse those fleshy growths purified, which are similar to the quill pen of a bird, so that nothing remains in them.
If however blood overcomes you, and flows between you and your operation, separating those fleshy growths: then it is better to do what is done, and for the sake of swift healing, to cauterize it with fire, or with acute medicine.
Since cauterizing with fire gathers good habits, to the purification of those added fleshy growths, and to the stopping of blood, and to the drying of moistures.
Then treat it with liniments wrapped in butter, or with triturated onions, until the place emits pus, and those purified fleshy growths emerge in the pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating salves, generating hard flesh: and there are medicines in which there are astringents and drying.
For when you restore, then already it will be healed; and not in vain repetition.
If, however, the fistula has already reached deep into the anus and is prolonged by the excess of the body: then insert your finger into the anus and examine it with that.
If you feel a tension, and between you and it there is a thin layer of sifac or flesh, and it is close to penetrating: then it is not an operation on that, unless according to the way of trust and hope.
That is, because one of the three methods is administered in it: either you cauterize it, as we said: or you dissect it, until you arrive at its concavity, so that it is possible for you to introduce a license and a cure from what is nearest. And you do not proceed much with the cutting, so that you do not injure the surrounding tissue of the anus, and there is no harm to the weak exit of the evacuation without control. Then treat it with what we have said.
Perhaps it will be healed: or you will prolong it with a thin layer, and cleanse it after you have cut it up to the anus, as we said, or with a tent or with another instrument of the acute extremity. Then cleanse those filtered flesh wounds which are in the cutting, until where you are able to do so with careful examination.
Then try to restore the whole wound with the cutting, and the upper orifice where it is consolidated: and a open fistula will remain in the inner part of the anus, and it will be lighter on the weak.
And sometimes the fistula follows this method: and it is when you insert a tent into the fistula: and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with the skin and edge of the anus: then receive the perforated extremity of the tent, which is like a needle, that is, preparing the leather, according to this form. And insert into it a twisted thread made from five threads, and wrap around it. Then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula, until it reaches its concavity.
If it is penetrating to the margin of the anus internally near, then extract the thread from that orifice: just as you insert your finger into the anus and extract the end of the thread, and join the two ends together: and tie them both, and leave it for one day or two days: and the more the thread penetrates into the flesh, tighten it well, until those fleshes which are between the two ends of the thread meet and fall away: then cure the wound, until it consolidates and heals.
But if the orifice of the fistula does not penetrate: then make it penetrate by whatever means are prepared for you, unless it is deeply situated. For it is not fitting for you to do that on account of the ligature, lest you injure it.
Then do with it as we have said, until it heals.
You should make a spoon-shaped instrument for the spiny fistula, whose curvature is acute and very sharp, and the other part is not acute, so that it does not injure what is not necessary, as you see.
Chapter 81.
Concerning the suturing of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows out from the incision of these: and the treatment of fissures.
There are hemorrhoids in two modes. Or they are inside the anus, like small bladders of carbon, or pomegranates: or as if they were grains of a grape. And among them there are small ones and large ones: and blood flows out from them always, and it is one, and they are many. And they are outside the anus, and on its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus are, for the most part, of scanty humidity, from which a watery discharge flows, or a little blood in a steady flow: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of that which is within the anus is to press on the weakened area so that it may be felt: and it should be pressed until it comes out of the anus, and the stringy fibers of the thigh appear. Therefore, you should hang it with hooks: or hold them with your fingernail. Then cut them off at their roots.
If however they are not retained by the hooks, due to their moisture and softness: then seize them with rough cloth, or with a double-layered linen bandage, and extract them with your fingers. Then cut them off, and sprinkle some hot powders over them after the incision, so that they may take the place of a cautery. Or cauterize them according to what was previously mentioned in the chapter on cauterization. Then treat them with the remaining treatment, until they are healed.
If the anus does not obey the evacuation, then inject a weak enema into the rectum, where there is a small bite, so that it may be washed out with what is in the anus, and it may quickly obey the evacuation, when the weakened area expresses itself.
If however the stringy fibers are external to the anus, then their removal is easy, effortless: and it is as if you grasp them with your fingernail, or grasp them with a hook, and cut them off. Then treat them with what we have said, until they are healed.
And for those who shy away from the incision with iron, then it is necessary to administer their suture according to this method. Take a twisted thread, and insert it into the point. Then draw out the stringy fibers upwards, and make it penetrate with the needle at its root on the other side: and twist the two ends of the thread at the lower part of the needle, and let them be transverse: and constrict the stringy fibers with a strong binding. Then tie a knot in the thread, and extract the needle.
Make an incision with all the athletic (muscular) strength, and let out one of them: nor press it yourself, so that it flows out with a surplus of blood.
Then put on the wound a piece of cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate, and place it on the wound: and apply pressure to the weak area, so that it quiets. Then let it fall off by itself, until it drops away.
When therefore the athletic (muscular) strength falls away, treat them with ointments and the remaining treatment, until they are healed.
On the treatment of fissures. For they often occur due to dryness of the feces and constriction of nature.
When therefore they become old and medicine is of no avail in them: then it is necessary to scrape them with the point of a spatula or with your finger, until they become moist, and the outer cortex which prevents their consolidation is removed. Then treat them, until they consolidate according to what is fitting.
If they do not consolidate: then treat them again with a more vigorous scraping than before, until they bleed much and are cleansed; then treat them until they are healed.
On the treatment of inverted hernias and not of inverted ones: and of muscular ruptures and of wounds caused by friction.
Chapter 82.
You know that a hernia is nothing but a rounded knot according to the color of the body, similar to the head of a nail: and it occurs throughout the entire body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and toes: and it causes pain when walking.
It is necessary therefore to cut what is around the nail, and to hold it with forceps or with a hook, and to eradicate it from its root.
Then treat that: and if you want to cauterize that according to what was mentioned previously in its chapter.
One of them is a small, rough, flaky, rounded elevation on the surface of the body. And they often occur on the hands of children.
And its treatment is to stretch out the elevation, and to cut into it, or to tie it with a silk thread, or with a hair, until it falls off. And if you wish, cauterize it according to what has been previously mentioned with fire, or with a sharp medicine, and now the inverted elevations are eradicated, and not the inverted ones with the instrument that I will describe.
A small flaky elevation is also a rough, superficial growth on the body, eating deeply into the skin; and when it finds cold, it feels like the sting of an ant, and it causes pain throughout the whole body; and mostly it occurs on the hands.
And its treatment is to take a small tube made from the feather of a goose or a strong vulture's feather, and place that tube over the ant-like growth, until it encircles with the parts of the tube. Then revolve your hand with the tube, until you squeeze out what is around the ant-like growth; and put it deep into the flesh, and eradicate the ant-like growth from its root.
And if you wish, make that with a tube of copper or iron, according to this method.
Let the upper part of the tube be applied to the limit of the swelling, drawing out what is beneath, so that it may be alleviated above the finger and its own rotation.
And if you wish, cauterize the ant-like growth according to what has been previously mentioned in the chapter on cauterization of Elevation.
Chapter 83.
Concerning the forms of instruments which are administered for enemas in ailments of the anus, and solutions of the belly, and colic.
Sometimes the enema instrument is made of silver, or of gold alloy, or of fused copper, or of hammered metal.
And when it is made small from these instruments, and large, according to those in which they are administered.
Therefore, that which is administered in the treatment of small children, let it be small: and for those whose veins are weak or painful, thus also their enemas.
A large enema.
The tube of it, that is, the upper part where the ligature is tied, should be large according to this method: and let there be a distinction so that the ligature is tied as you see, and the lower end which is inserted into the anus, should be blunt, that is, not open, gentle, indeed, drawing towards subtlety: and on one side of it there should be two openings, and on the other side an opening.
And let the width of the openings be according to the thickness of the radices, and let it be thicker for a small one, and let there be an intestine in which medicines are placed from the bladder of an animal: or from the paper of an owl, which should be according to the form of a small asafoetida: whose root is one palm.
And let it be pierced with many openings as it revolves, and let there be a space that is between all the openings the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those openings a strong thread made from raw thread, which should be of ten threads, or around that, and tie it with the intestine like an asafoetida. When therefore the intestine is placed in it, let it be tied at the head of the enema between two distinct constrictions with a strong binding. Then inject the enema with it.
And this is the form of a circle as depicted here, and of the openings.
The quality of injecting with it, however, is: that you should fill the intestine, or bladder, with a medicine which is warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the sick person: and take care that it not be too hot, nor too cold.
Then the weak patient is placed on his back, and his thighs are elevated to a higher position: and a soft cloth, that is, a cushion, is put underneath him, on which the men who are performing the operation sit.
Then anoint the extremities with a cluster of olives, or with album gypsum, or with foeniculi of galbanum, or similar. Then introduce it into the anus with ease. Then the assistant should take the uterus with both his hands at once, and press it out with great force, until everything that is in the Cluster (enema) goes into the intestine.
Then withdraw the cluster, and elevate the patient's thighs to the wall.
What if the medicine thinks it is going to an exit, then he should hold on as much as he can. And if he sleeps with it the whole night, it is more useful in the treatment.
If, however, you cluster him in the solutions of the belly's agitations, and hasten his evacuation: then repeat the clustering until he is healed.
What if there are hemorrhoids in the anus, or painful apostemes, then let the clustering be gentle, mild, from the clusterings with which children are clustered.
And this should be the form of gentle clustering upon a constricted skin.
Head 83.
Now I have spoken in the division on the treatment of wounds that it was fitting for the book, and I will say here their treatment with manual handling, and with medicines according to their completion.
I say therefore that wounds are diversified according to the thing by which they are made, and according to the place upon which the wound falls.
There are therefore many ways in which wounds are made, such as a blow of a stone, or a cut of a sword, or a stab of a dagger, or a strike with a lance, or a wood, or an arrow: and similar things from many other causes.
Wounds that are inflicted according to the location of the body are, such as a wound that falls on the head, or neck, or chest, or belly, or liver: and similar ones from these members.
And I am describing the treatments of certain wounds, so that I may establish a reasoning and rule about the remaining wounds.
And I begin with simple head wounds, because the recollection of the composite wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
I say therefore. When a simple wound occurs on the head, and there is no fracture of the bone: consider then if it is from a blow of a stone or similar things, and has only bruised the skin: and it is a great wound, and there is a tendency to inflame the weak aposteme with hot swelling: then hasten, and perform phlebotomy on the head immediately: and do not delay: and extract from him as much blood as his strength allows, according to the quantity of his virtue: if nothing prohibits phlebotomy, especially if the blood that flows out of the wound is scant. And let the phlebotomy be from the opposite part of the wounded area.
And let the phlebotomy be from the opposite part of the wounded area. And let the weak person beware of repletion, and wine, and coarse foods.
If something prohibits moderation, then let it be diminished from food, and not approach flesh, nor wine.
And apply to the wound if it happens to have a hot aposteme, a cloth soaked in rose oil alone, or with wine in which there is stipation.
If you have been free from the hot aposteme, then apply to the wound, if it is fresh with its own blood, and has not changed the air, a powder which I will describe shortly: and if it has already changed the air, then apply to it certain ointments, until it is healed.
If the wound is large, or it is from an incised wound, and similar: and its lips do not adhere through granulations, then they are joined together with a suture, according to what I will describe about the sutures of wounds in the belly.
If the wound is already opened up to the bone, and it is hanging, and there is no retention of it, except in a small suspension: then incise it. Then treat the wound with medications, and restore to it hard flesh in place of skin, and prescribe to the weak person, that they take nourishing foods in which there is richness, such as are heads, and cooked wheat, until it be like a pulse: and similar things.
If you find putrefaction in the skin, and it does not adhere to the bone: then incise the entire putrefied area, and cast it away: then treat what remains.
If however in these wounds there is an artery, or a vein from which blood flows: and it does not stop by means of medications, then make a ligature above the artery. If therefore you find it is not cut, then dry it with a cautery, or tie it off. If necessity demands when what we have said does not help, then cauterize it, until the blood is staunched.
If however the wounds are small, simple, then their treatment is easy, light: so that you dust them with this powder: because it consolidates them before they suppurate.
The method of applying the incarnative powder. Take one part of olibanum, and two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unextinguished lime: grind everything into a fine powder, and sift it: and fill the wound with it, and constrict it with a good bandage, until it adheres well to the wound, and coagulates with the blood.
Then tie it above with a compress and leave it, and do not loosen it as long as it remains, so that it does not become inflamed. For it is not eradicated by medicine, until it is healed.
And when it makes a hard crust alone, when you do not have olive oil present, and dragon's blood also performs the same operation in many large wounds, when it is suitable to apply it to them and bind them, and they are fresh wounds with their own blood, which has not changed in the air.
For if the air has already changed them through some alteration, especially when it is in the summer season, then there is no purpose in applying this powder: therefore take care of it with what we have said, so that you apply to them certain digestive ointments: or apply to them poultices made from barley flour, prepared with water and honey, until they discharge pus. Then take care of the remaining treatment, until they are healed.
If it happens to be a fracture of the bone with a wound, and it is small, then extract it with gestures; and I will now describe the treatment of head fractures in what follows.
On wounds of the neck.
If a wound occurs on the neck, then there is no difference between it and head wounds when they are simple.
If the nerve of the neck is injured, or an artery: then if it is a nerve, there is no ingenuity in it, unless one tries to heal it with what causes strong stitching, such as zinc, and zeig, and similar things. Because they harm the nerves and constrict them.
And do not apply anything cold to the wound at all: because the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the most sublime of the membranes: and it is thus that it should be treated with gentle medicines, such as lota calcium dissolved in sweet water many times infused with oil, or with rose oil, and tuthia, when washing also with sweet water: and other mineral stones, according to this method, and humid ointments.
If the wound is large, then apply a suture: or bind the lips of it with small pillows. Then take care of it, until it heals.
If the wound is deep, or if a sinus has formed in its lower part, where pus has already gathered, then pierce it in a more depressed place.
If an artery has been cut in the wound and its blood flow has followed: then separate or ligate it, and bind it: or cauterize it, if necessity demands it.
If the vertebrae of the neck or all of them are broken, and the wound is safe: then gather the lips of the skin with a suture above the cane of the neck, and do not touch the neck, but equalize it, and reduce it to its natural shape. Then bind it with a suitable bandage, and leave it for several days. Then take care of it with ointments in which there is strengthening and drying, until it heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then investigate it: then if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all of them, or as many as you can: and what cannot be prepared, leave that until the wound putrefies, and separates and alleviates its discharge.
If the wound is fresh, then powder over it with the powder that I described. If a hole is seen in the bone of the wound, and it becomes a fistula: then take care of it with that which was mentioned in its chapter.
On wounds on the shoulder blade.
If it is a wound from a lance or a knife: and you see its depth, then consider it. If therefore bad air comes out of the wound, when the weak person exhales from it, then know that the wound is mortal.
What if there is no depth to it and it is fresh with its own blood? Then you should not apply powder to it at the first hour, nor bind it tightly, so that the blood is not retained in its depth and returns to the heart, and kills the weak person. But put an attracting ointment on it, and loosen it during the day twice.
If you do not have an ointment at hand, then put a clean cloth on the opening of the wound, so that it absorbs what flows out from the humidity. And let the weak person sleep on the wound, so that what accumulates in it runs clear.
If already three days or more have passed since the wound, and no spasm has occurred to the weak person, nor evil tremor of the heart, nor constriction in breathing, and you see the other good dispositions of it: then know that the wound is healthy. Therefore treat it with liniments and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
If indeed the healing of it is hindered, and it always opens up, then know that a fistula has been made. Therefore treat it from its head.
And if the wound is from a thrusting injury or a knife, and it is simple on the surface of the chest or back: then treat it with what was mentioned before about suturing, if it is large: or with powder, if it is small.
If however it has made an impression on the bone, and a fragment has broken off from it: then probe the wound, and prepare to extract that fragment, if they are separate. If however they are not separate, then leave them alone, until the wound putrefies, for their extraction is of no benefit.
The judgment of the other accidental wounds in the remaining limbs in treatment is the same as what we have said.
Concerning wounds of the abdomen and the exit of the intestines, and their treatment.
The disruptions that occur in the belly are great, moderate, and small.
From the great ones, it happens when the intestine protrudes or a number of intestines.
Therefore their insertion is more violent and difficult, and their suture.
And a small disruption also becomes difficult in another way. It follows, therefore, that their reduction is more difficult, if you do not promptly return them to their place during the introduction itself: because they become swollen, open up, and enlarge; hence their entry becomes difficult.
On account of this, therefore, a moderate disruption is better: because when there is no difficult reduction of the intestine, as it is dissimilar in these two species.
You know that the suture of the belly is according to four modes.
Two common sutures are suitable for the suture of the belly and for the suture of other wounds of the body; and two other sutures specifically communicate with remaining wounds. However, they are more proper for the suture of the belly; and I will tell you each one with explanation and declaration.
I say therefore, because when the wound is small and something protrudes from it out of the intestine, and it becomes difficult to reduce it; then that is on account of one of two modes. Or because of the smallness of the disruption, as we have said; or because there is inflammation in the intestine on account of the coldness of the air.
