And the sign of its dislocation is that you will notice the injured person applies their leg to their hip. If it does not adhere to the hip: then you know that the knee is dislocated.
And the restoration of all modes of its dislocation is to make the injured person sit upright, so that they can now stretch out their leg if they can on it, and adhere your back to their face: and put their foot between your feet.
Then adhere to its knee with your palms, and place them straight between your fingers over its knee. Then apply both sides of your palm to its knee with strength. And another person should stretch out its foot, until its knee returns to its place.
And the sign of reduction is that the leg adheres to the hip with gentleness, not painfully.
Then apply a plaster to it, and make the leg adhere to the hip. Then bind them together with a bandage for three days or four. Then release it.
And let the patient not use it for walking for several days, until it heals.
If, however, the reduction is refused to you, then administer a strong extension with ligaments, whose preceding narrative was in the treatment of dislocation, until it returns.
On the treatment of dislocation of the ankle bone.
The ankle bone is sometimes removed with a small removal, and sometimes it is dislocated according to its completeness. And its dislocation occurs either inward or outward.
And the sign of its dislocation is that you see the ankle bone swollen, proceeding to the part towards which it is dislocated.
The treatment of its removal, however, is an easy reduction: and it is, that it should be extended with ease by hand, and adjusted, until it returns.
In the treatment of it when it is dislocated according to its completeness, it is necessary that you make the patient sit upright; and another strong assistant should hold it firmly from behind, at the middle of his back.
Then you should hold with your right hand its foot from the upper part of it, and with your left hand from the lower part of its heel at the ankle's place.
Then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand. Then with the left [hand] and two fingers.
Then stretch out with the left [hand], and strike the heel of the foot with the right [hand], turning the leg without exertion.
Do that twice, as we have narrated.
Then strike the heel of the foot towards the leg at the third stroke, and you will draw out the shaft.
If it returns to its place at the first stroke, or at the second according to this method, and you see the foot is straightened, it is good; and if not, then repeat the operation over it: for it will return itself.
If, however, the reduction of it is prohibited to you with what we have narrated: then make the weak part rest on its back on the ground, and fix a small peg firmly in the earth, so that it falls between its hips; and you have already wrapped a cloth around it, so that it does not harm the weak part.
Then a helper should take hold of its hip; afterwards another helper stretches out the foot, either with their hands or with a bandage that binds above the ankle. Then each helper stretches out against the extension of their companion; and the small peg stands between the two hips of the weak part, holding it, so that its body is not pulled downwards at the extension.
Then the physician adjusts the dislocation with his hands, and another helper holds the healthy leg downwards. For the dislocation returns with swiftness.
When therefore the dislocation returns, and the health of its reduction is declared to you: then put on a plaster and padding, and bind it firmly with ligatures, and tie the foot with a bandage to the leg.
And it is necessary to beware lest you bind the nerves which are behind the heel, so that the bandage does not press upon them violently and harms them.
Then leave it for two days, or three. What if the bandage is softened? Tighten it; then loosen it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for forty days. If however the patient is allowed to walk before that time, there will not be security unless the dislocation is dissolved over it, and it becomes corrupted, and does not receive a cure after that.
What if a hot abscess happens to him: then it is necessary to administer to him the treatment that we previously mentioned in another place for its cure, and fomentation, until it is removed.
On the Dislocation of Toes and their Treatment.
It is necessary that what is dislocated is adjusted with a few gentle extensions without strain, and this indeed is not difficult, but rather easy.
If the dislocation is in certain nodes of the back of the foot, then it is necessary that the patient sit with his foot on a level place on the ground or on a stool, and stand as if walking.
Then you stand, and put your foot on what protrudes from those joints. Then press it with your foot with force, until it returns to its place, and you will see that it is already adjusted, and does not appear prominent in its location.
Then put under the foot a stool that captures the whole foot, which has two heads. Then tighten it with a suitable bandage for three days. Then loosen it, and make him rest from walking for many days, until it is strengthened and secured from the dislocation.
On the types of dislocation with wound or fracture.
When something happens from that, and you strive for its cure and his restoration, many times death occurs; and because of this, it is not fitting to presume upon its cure, which is of this sort, unless one who is prudent in the art, long-experienced, merciful, pious, slow, not daring, nor presumptuous; and that he should use medicinal measures that soothe only hot abscesses; and leave the patient to divine judgment. Unless you despair, or hope for health with mildness of chronic illness, and in which something of hope appears. Take care therefore to reduce it at once from the beginning of the disease, before a warm abscess forms.
If therefore the limb returns to health, according to what you wished, then administer the regime that soothes the abscess: and treat the wound with what is suitable for it from drying ointments.
What if there is dislocation with fracture, and it occurs in separated bones, then take care to reset them, and do in that what we said in simple chronic illnesses from what preceded in their places.
And beware according to your ability, and guard yourself from the entrance into the way of fear: according to what preceded my prediction to you.
For that is better for you with your Creator, and more permanent to your glory, and more healthful to your body among those in your time.
